# Babylon's Wine: The Hidden Legacy and God's Final Call

**A comprehensive examination of how human tradition replaced biblical truth—and the prophetic call to return**

---

## A Word to the Sincere Reader

If you're reading this document, you likely love God and desire to follow His truth. This study is not written to condemn but to inform; not to attack but to enlighten. Many who compiled this material once held traditional church teachings without questioning their biblical foundation. Discovering what Scripture actually says—compared to what we were taught—was challenging but ultimately liberating.

The Bible distinguishes between **Babylon the system** (which God condemns) and **"My people" in Babylon** (whom God lovingly calls out). Revelation 18:4 says, "Come out of her, **my people**, lest you share in her sins." God has faithful, sincere believers in every denomination who love Him deeply but have inherited traditions they never questioned.

This document asks you to examine whether your beliefs rest on **biblical authority** or **human tradition**—not to judge your sincerity, but to help you align with God's Word. The antichrist identification in this study is not meant to condemn individuals within the system, but to recognize the system itself that has led billions away from biblical truth. Understanding who the antichrist is helps us recognize the system we need to come out of, while maintaining love and respect for those still within it.

Study prayerfully, search the Scriptures (Acts 17:11), and ask the Holy Spirit for guidance (John 16:13). Truth may be uncomfortable initially, but it brings freedom (John 8:32).

---

## Important Clarifications

### Biblical Authority: The Foundation of Everything

**This guide relies on the Bible and the Bible alone as its authority.** Every doctrine, every claim, every conclusion must be tested against Scripture. No human authority—no church, no tradition, no theologian, no denomination—can override what God has plainly revealed in His Word.

> **Isaiah 8:20** - "To the law and to the testimony! If they do not speak according to this word, it is because there is no light in them."

> **Acts 17:11** - "These were more fair-minded than those in Thessalonica, in that they received the word with all readiness, and searched the Scriptures daily to find out whether these things were so."

> **2 Timothy 3:16-17** - "All Scripture is given by inspiration of God, and is profitable for doctrine, for reproof, for correction, for instruction in righteousness, that the man of God may be complete, thoroughly equipped for every good work."

**Test everything you read here against God's Word.** If something in this guide contradicts Scripture, reject it. If it aligns with Scripture, accept it—regardless of how it challenges your current beliefs or traditions.

### These Are Biblical Truths, Not Denominational Teachings

The doctrines presented in this study are **not the invention of any modern denomination**. These truths include:

- **Obedience to God's commandments** - All of them, not just the ones tradition has kept (Matthew 5:18-19; Revelation 14:12)
- **The identity of the antichrist system** - Recognized by virtually all Protestant Reformers (Luther, Calvin, Wesley, Knox, Tyndale, etc.) as the papal system
- **The state of the dead** - That the dead "know nothing" (Ecclesiastes 9:5) and await resurrection
- **Salvation by grace through faith** - Not by works or human tradition (Ephesians 2:8-9)
- **The immutability of God's law** - That not one jot or tittle passes from the law (Matthew 5:18)

These biblical truths existed **long before any modern church organization**. They were taught by the prophets, affirmed by Jesus, proclaimed by the apostles, and rediscovered by Reformers throughout history.

### This Message Is for Everyone

**You don't need to belong to any specific denomination to understand and embrace biblical truth.** God has faithful people in every church and tradition who are sincerely seeking Him. This study simply asks you to examine **what the Bible actually says** versus **what human tradition has taught**.

> **Revelation 18:4** - "And I heard another voice from heaven saying, 'Come out of her, my people, lest you share in her sins, and lest you receive of her plagues.'"

Notice God says **"my people"** are still in Babylon—sincere believers who haven't yet discovered these truths. God is calling them **out of the system**, not condemning their sincerity.

**After studying this guide:**
1. **Test everything against Scripture** - Don't take anyone's word for it
2. **Ask the Holy Spirit for guidance** - He promises to lead you into all truth (John 16:13)
3. **Search for a church that teaches and practices these biblical truths** - Find a community that bases doctrine on Scripture alone, keeps all of God's commandments as He gave them, and proclaims the messages of Revelation 14:6-12
4. **Be willing to follow wherever God leads** - Even if it means leaving cherished traditions behind

### Truth Transcends Denomination

The truths in this study are **not denominationally branded**—they're biblically revealed. They belong to God, not to any human organization. Whether you're Catholic, Baptist, Methodist, Pentecostal, non-denominational, or from any other background, **the question is not "What does my church teach?" but "What does the Bible teach?"**

**Historical Reality**: These truths have been proclaimed by faithful believers throughout history—Waldenses in medieval Europe, Reformers during the Protestant Reformation, and various movements since then. God has always had a faithful remnant who cling to His Word despite opposition.

### The Mental and Physical Health Crisis and Biblical Truth Connection

We live in unprecedented times of health collapse:
- **Depression has increased 300% since 2010**
- **Anxiety affects 31% of teenagers**
- **Diabetes has doubled globally since 1980**
- **Cancer rates continue rising despite medical advances**
- **Heart disease remains the #1 killer worldwide**
- **Autoimmune diseases are at epidemic levels**

Despite medical improvements, disease far outweighs treatment advances. These crises are not coincidental—they result from abandoning biblical principles of health (nutrition, media consumption, and spiritual obedience). When we reject God's design for how we should live, we suffer the consequences physically, mentally, and spiritually.

**Biblical health principles + spiritual obedience = the clarity and strength needed to stand for truth in the final crisis.**

### A Warning About the Final Test

This study reveals that **obedience to God's law will be the final test of loyalty**—will you follow what God commands or what human tradition teaches? But here's what many miss:

**You cannot pass the final test if your brain is compromised by:**
- Poor nutrition that suppresses frontal lobe function (see Daniel Diet guide)
- Media consumption that hijacks moral discernment (see Media Influence guide)
- Spiritual compromise that weakens your connection to God (this guide)

All three areas must be addressed. You cannot separate physical health from spiritual faithfulness. Daniel understood this—he refused the king's rich food **before** he faced the test of worshiping the golden image (Daniel 1, then Daniel 3). **The diet came first because he needed a clear mind to stand firm later.**

### **The Biblical Method: Precept Upon Precept**

Before examining any doctrine, we must understand **how** to study Scripture correctly. God Himself provides the method:

> **Isaiah 28:10** - "For precept must be upon precept, precept upon precept, line upon line, line upon line, here a little, there a little."

**What This Means**:

This verse reveals the foundational principle of biblical interpretation: **Scripture interprets Scripture**. Truth is established by comparing multiple passages across the entire Bible, not by isolating a single verse.

**The Principle in Practice**:

1. **"Precept upon precept"** - One biblical teaching built on another
2. **"Line upon line"** - Multiple scriptures compared and harmonized
3. **"Here a little, there a little"** - Truth gathered from throughout the Bible

**Why This Matters**:

- **Single verses can be misinterpreted** - taken out of context or twisted to support false doctrine
- **The whole Bible must harmonize** - if your interpretation of one verse contradicts clear teaching elsewhere, you've misunderstood
- **False teachers use isolated verses** - pulling single texts while ignoring contradictory passages
- **God's truth is consistent** - Scripture never contradicts Scripture when properly understood

**Biblical Warnings**:

> **2 Peter 3:16** - Speaking of Paul's letters: "in which are some things hard to understand, which **untaught and unstable people twist to their own destruction**, as they do also the rest of the Scriptures."

> **2 Timothy 2:15** - "Be diligent to present yourself approved to God, a worker who does not need to be ashamed, **rightly dividing the word of truth**."

**Application to This Study**:

Throughout this document, you'll see teachings examined using **multiple Scripture passages** that **harmonize together**. When someone quotes a single verse to defend a doctrine, but that doctrine contradicts clear teaching found in many other passages, the **harmony of Scripture** reveals which interpretation is correct.

For example, if a doctrine:
- Depends on **one or two isolated verses** while contradicting numerous clear passages elsewhere
- Requires **complicated explanations** to reconcile with the rest of Scripture
- Forces you to **ignore** or **reinterpret** many straightforward biblical statements

Then the doctrine likely rests on human tradition rather than biblical truth.

**The Test**: Does your doctrine harmonize with the **entire counsel of God** (Acts 20:27), or does it depend on isolated verses while ignoring contradictory passages?

This is why we examine each topic with **extensive Scripture comparison**—allowing the Bible to interpret itself, "precept upon precept, line upon line."

### **Biblical Foundation for This Appeal**:

> **Acts 17:11** - "These were more fair-minded than those in Thessalonica, in that they received the word with all readiness, and **searched the Scriptures daily** to find out whether these things were so."

> **John 16:13** - "However, when He, the Spirit of truth, has come, **He will guide you into all truth**; for He will not speak on His own authority, but whatever He hears He will speak; and He will tell you things to come."

> **John 8:32** - "And you shall know the truth, and **the truth shall make you free**."

> **Acts 20:27** - "For I have not shunned to declare to you **the whole counsel of God**."

> **James 1:22** - "But be **doers of the word, and not hearers only**, deceiving yourselves."

This final verse is crucial: discovering biblical truth is only the beginning. Once you see what God's Word actually teaches, will you have the courage to **act on it**—even if it means leaving cherished traditions behind? Many will read this document, see the evidence, yet continue in traditions because change feels too difficult. But God calls us to be **doers**, not just hearers. The question is not just "What does the Bible say?" but "Will I obey what it says?"

### **The Eternal Consequences**

The stakes could not be higher. When Jesus returns, there will be only two responses from Him:

**The Warning**:

> **Matthew 7:23** - "And then I will declare to them, '**I never knew you; depart from Me, you who practice lawlessness!**'"

> **Mark 3:29** - "but he who blasphemes against the Holy Spirit **never has forgiveness, but is subject to eternal condemnation**."

> **Matthew 12:31-32** - "Therefore I say to you, every sin and blasphemy will be forgiven men, but **the blasphemy against the Spirit will not be forgiven** men. Anyone who speaks a word against the Son of Man, it will be forgiven him; but whoever speaks against the Holy Spirit, it will not be forgiven him, either in this age or in the age to come."

These are perhaps the most sobering verses in Scripture. To reject the Holy Spirit's conviction—to see biblical truth clearly yet choose tradition over obedience—is to blaspheme against the Spirit who brought you that truth.

**The Hope**:

> **Matthew 25:21** - "His lord said to him, '**Well done, good and faithful servant**; you were faithful over a few things, I will make you ruler over many things. Enter into the joy of your lord.'"

Which words will you hear when Jesus returns? The choice is yours. This document presents biblical evidence. The Holy Spirit will convict your heart. Will you be a **doer** of the word, or only a hearer?

## The 7-Day Week Cycle

### Has the 7-Day Cycle Ever Changed?

**No**, the 7-day week cycle has been **remarkably stable** for over 2,000 years in cultures that adopted it. There's no recorded instance of the cycle "skipping" or resetting (unlike when calendars switched from Julian to Gregorian, which dropped days but kept the weekly cycle intact).

### Origins of the 7-Day Week

- **Babylonian** (~600 BCE): Based on lunar phases and 7 visible celestial bodies
- **Jewish**: Adopted early, with Sabbath as the 7th day
- **Roman Empire** (1st-4th century CE): Spread the 7-day week throughout Europe

### Day Names Throughout History

#### Babylonian (Celestial Bodies)
1. Sun
2. Moon
3. Mars
4. Mercury
5. Jupiter
6. Venus
7. Saturn

#### Roman (Latin - Planetary Gods)
1. Dies Solis (Sun)
2. Dies Lunae (Moon)
3. Dies Martis (Mars)
4. Dies Mercurii (Mercury)
5. Dies Iovis (Jupiter)
6. Dies Veneris (Venus)
7. Dies Saturni (Saturn)

#### Old English (Germanic Gods Replaced Roman Ones)
1. Sunnandæg (Sun's day)
2. Mōnandæg (Moon's day)
3. Tīwesdæg (Tiw/Tyr's day)
4. Wōdnesdæg (Woden/Odin's day)
5. Þūnresdæg (Thor's day)
6. Frīgedæg (Frigg/Freya's day)
7. Sæternesdæg (Saturn's day)

#### Modern English
1. Sunday
2. Monday
3. Tuesday (Tiw/Tyr)
4. Wednesday (Woden/Odin)
5. Thursday (Thor)
6. Friday (Frigg/Freya)
7. Saturday

**Note**: Romance languages kept Roman names (e.g., Spanish: Lunes=Moon, Martes=Mars), while Germanic languages substituted their own gods.

---

**What are Romance Languages?** 
Romance languages are languages that evolved from Latin, the language of the Roman Empire. They are called "Romance" because they descended from the **Roman** language. Major Romance languages include:
- **Spanish** (Spain, Latin America)
- **French** (France)
- **Italian** (Italy)
- **Portuguese** (Portugal, Brazil)
- **Romanian** (Romania)

These languages preserved the Roman planetary/god names for weekdays (e.g., Spanish: Lunes=Moon, Martes=Mars, Miércoles=Mercury, Jueves=Jupiter, Viernes=Venus). In contrast, **Germanic languages** (English, German, Dutch, Norse languages) replaced Roman god names with their own Germanic gods (Tuesday=Tiw's day, Wednesday=Woden's day, Thursday=Thor's day, Friday=Frigg's day).

---

### Saturday = Sabbath: Linguistic Testimony Across the World

**One of the most powerful witnesses to the biblical seventh-day Sabbath is language itself**. Throughout the world, in over **100 languages**, the seventh day of the week is called by a word meaning **"Sabbath"** or derived from the Hebrew word *Shabbat*.

This linguistic evidence proves that humanity has historically recognized Saturday as the Sabbath day, and this knowledge has been preserved in the very names of languages across continents.

#### **Languages That Call Saturday "Sabbath"**

**Romance Languages** (descended from Latin):
- **Spanish**: *Sábado* (Sabbath)
- **Portuguese**: *Sábado* (Sabbath)
- **Italian**: *Sabato* (Sabbath)
- **Romanian**: *Sâmbătă* (Sabbath)
- **Catalan**: *Dissabte* (Sabbath day)

**Slavic Languages**:
- **Russian**: *Суббота* (*Subbota*) (Sabbath)
- **Polish**: *Sobota* (Sabbath)
- **Czech**: *Sobota* (Sabbath)
- **Bulgarian**: *Събота* (*Sabota*) (Sabbath)
- **Serbian/Croatian**: *Субота/Subota* (Sabbath)
- **Slovak**: *Sobota* (Sabbath)
- **Ukrainian**: *Субота* (*Subota*) (Sabbath)

**Greek**:
- **Modern Greek**: *Σάββατο* (*Sávvato*) (Sabbath)
- **Ancient Greek**: *Σάββατον* (*Sabbaton*) (Sabbath) - same word used throughout New Testament

**Middle Eastern Languages**:
- **Hebrew**: *שַׁבָּת* (*Shabbat*) (Sabbath) - the original
- **Arabic**: *السبت* (*As-Sabt*) (The Sabbath)
- **Aramaic**: *Šabbəṯā* (Sabbath)
- **Persian**: *شنبه* (*Shanbeh*) (Sabbath)

**Asian Languages**:
- **Indonesian**: *Sabtu* (Sabbath)
- **Malay**: *Sabtu* (Sabbath)
- **Tagalog** (Philippines): *Sabado* (Sabbath)

**African Languages**:
- **Swahili**: *Jumamosi* (literally "Sabbath day")
- **Amharic** (Ethiopia): *ቅዳሜ* (*Kidame*) - related to Sabbath concept
- **Hausa**: *Asabar* (Sabbath)

**European Languages**:
- **Armenian**: *Շաբաթ* (*Shabat*) (Sabbath)
- **Georgian**: *შაბათი* (*Shabati*) (Sabbath)
- **Hungarian**: *Szombat* (Sabbath)
- **Bosnian**: *Subota* (Sabbath)

**Note**: Even languages that don't use "Sabbath" for Saturday often use it in religious contexts. For example, **French** uses *Samedi* (from Saturn's day) for the civil day, but refers to the biblical Sabbath as *Sabbat*.

#### **The Significance of This Linguistic Evidence**

**1. Universal Testimony**:
Languages spanning Europe, Asia, Africa, and the Middle East—representing different language families (Romance, Slavic, Semitic, Germanic)—all testify that the seventh day is the **Sabbath**.

**2. Preserved Through History**:
These language names developed over **centuries and millennia**, preserving the knowledge that Saturday is the Sabbath long before modern denominational debates.

**3. Languages Don't Lie**:
While churches and traditions can change, **language preserves historical truth**. The fact that over 100 languages call Saturday "Sabbath" is irrefutable evidence that this was the universally recognized Sabbath day.

**4. Catholic Church's Own Admission**:
The Catholic Church changed the day of worship from Saturday to Sunday, yet even Romance languages (Spanish, Italian, Portuguese)—which developed in Catholic countries—**still call Saturday "Sabbath"**. The language itself contradicts the change.

**5. No Language Calls Sunday "Sabbath"**:
Significantly, **no language** traditionally calls Sunday by a word meaning "Sabbath." Sunday is called:
- **English**: Sunday (Sun's day)
- **Spanish**: Domingo (Lord's day)
- **Italian**: Domenica (Lord's day)
- **Portuguese**: Domingo (Lord's day)
- **French**: Dimanche (Lord's day)
- **German**: Sonntag (Sun day)
- **Russian**: Воскресенье (*Voskreseniye*) (Resurrection day)

Even the Catholic term "Lord's Day" (Domingo, Domenica, Dimanche) for Sunday is distinct from "Sabbath"—acknowledging that Sunday is **not** the Sabbath.

#### **Biblical Confirmation**

The New Testament, written in Greek, uses **Σάββατον** (*Sabbaton*) meaning "Sabbath" throughout:

- **Matthew 28:1**: "Now after the Sabbath [*Sabbaton*], as the first day of the week began to dawn..."
- **Mark 16:2**: "Very early in the morning, on the first day of the week, they came to the tomb when the sun had risen."
- **Luke 23:56**: "Then they returned and prepared spices and fragrant oils. And they rested on the Sabbath [*Sabbaton*] according to the commandment."
- **Acts 13:14**: "But when they departed from Perga, they came to Antioch in Pisidia, and went into the synagogue on the Sabbath [*Sabbaton*] day and sat down."

Greek clearly distinguished between:
- **Sabbath day** (*Sabbaton*) = Seventh day (Saturday)
- **First day of the week** (*Mia ton Sabbaton*) = Day after Sabbath (Sunday)

The New Testament **never** calls Sunday the "Sabbath."

#### **The Unchangeable Testimony**

**Languages across the world testify**: The seventh day is the **Sabbath**.

- Spanish speakers say *Sábado* (Sabbath)
- Italian speakers say *Sabato* (Sabbath)
- Russian speakers say *Суббота* (Sabbath)
- Greek speakers say *Σάββατο* (Sabbath)
- Arabic speakers say *السبت* (Sabbath)
- Over 100 languages preserve this truth

**Yet the church changed it to Sunday.**

This linguistic evidence alone should cause every sincere Christian to ask:
- Why do over 100 languages call Saturday "Sabbath"?
- Why does no language call Sunday "Sabbath"?
- If God changed the Sabbath to Sunday, why didn't languages change to reflect it?
- Could it be that language itself testifies to the truth—**Saturday is, and always has been, the Sabbath**?

**The world's languages bear witness**: God's Sabbath is the seventh day—**Saturday**—not Sunday.

---

## When Does a Day Start and End?

### Historical Day-Start Times by Culture

| Culture / Calendar | When the Day Begins |
|-------------------|---------------------|
| **Hebrew / Jewish** | Sunset (evening) |
| **Biblical** | Sunset (Genesis: "evening and morning") |
| **Babylonian** | Sunset |
| **Early Christian** | Sunset (following Jewish tradition) |
| **Greek (Athenian)** | Sunset |
| **Greek (Ionian)** | Sunrise |
| **Roman (Classical)** | Midnight (for civil purposes) |
| **Christian (post-Constantine)** | Midnight (adopted Roman civil practice) |
| **Islamic** | Sunset (Maghrib prayer time) |
| **Chinese traditional** | Near midnight (11 PM start of "Rat" hour) |
| **Modern civil (worldwide)** | Midnight (00:00) |

### Key Patterns

**Sunset Start**: Most ancient Near Eastern cultures
- Hebrew, Babylonian, Athenian, Islamic
- Practical for agricultural societies
- Aligns with natural transition from light to dark

**Sunrise Start**: Some Greek city-states, Ancient Egyptians
- Day begins with light/activity
- Natural alignment with work cycles

**Midnight Start**: Roman civil administration, modern worldwide
- Adopted by post-Constantine Christianity
- More practical for record-keeping and modern timekeeping
- No visible transition but mathematically precise

### Detailed Historical Systems

**Ancient Babylonian** (~2000 BCE):
- Day began at **sunset**
- Used in early Mesopotamian civilizations

**Ancient Egyptian**:
- Day began at **dawn/sunrise**
- 24-hour system with 12 daylight and 12 nighttime hours (seasonal length)

**Hebrew/Jewish** (still used):
- Day begins at **sunset** (around 6 PM)
- Based on Genesis: "evening and morning were the first day"
- Why Sabbath starts Friday evening

**Ancient Roman**:
- Originally at **sunrise**
- Later shifted to **midnight** for civil purposes

**Medieval Europe**:
- **Sunset** start was common
- Influenced by Christian liturgical hours
- Varied by region and purpose

**Islamic**:
- Day begins at **sunset** (Maghrib prayer time)
- Each Islamic date starts at sunset

**Chinese Traditional**:
- Day began at **midnight** (11 PM - 1 AM, the "Rat" hour)
- 12 two-hour periods named after zodiac animals

**Modern Standard**:
- Day starts at **midnight (00:00)** and ends at **23:59:59**
- Standardized for practical/administrative reasons
- Adopted gradually from 14th-19th centuries in Europe
- **Why midnight won**: Easier for record-keeping, business, and transportation schedules

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

## The Biblical Sabbath vs. Current Practice

### Biblical Sabbath

**When**: **7th day of the week** (Saturday)
- **Starts**: Friday at sunset
- **Ends**: Saturday at sunset
- **Duration**: ~24 hours

**Biblical Definition of a Day** (Evening to Evening):

The Bible clearly defines a day as beginning at sunset (evening) and ending at the next sunset:

- **Genesis 1:5**: "So the evening and the morning were the first day."
  - Pattern established at Creation: Evening (sunset) comes first, then morning
  - Each day of Creation week follows this pattern: "evening and morning"
  - Biblical day = sunset to sunset, not midnight to midnight

- **Leviticus 23:32**: "It shall be to you a sabbath of solemn rest, and you shall afflict your souls; on the ninth day of the month at evening, **from evening to evening**, you shall celebrate your sabbath."
  - Explicit instruction: Sabbath observance is "from evening to evening"
  - Confirms biblical day begins at sunset (evening)
  - Day of Atonement example applies to all biblical days

- **Nehemiah 13:19**: "So it was, at the gates of Jerusalem, as it began to be dark **before the Sabbath**, I commanded that the gates be shut, and charged that they must not be opened till after the Sabbath."
  - Nehemiah closed Jerusalem gates at sunset on Friday
  - "Before the Sabbath" = Friday at dark (sunset)
  - Confirms Sabbath begins Friday evening at sunset

**Key Principle**: The biblical day runs from **sunset to sunset**, not midnight to midnight (modern convention). This is why the seventh-day Sabbath begins Friday evening at sunset and ends Saturday evening at sunset.

**Biblical Foundation**:

- **Genesis 2:2-3**: "And on the seventh day God ended His work which He had done, and He rested on the seventh day from all His work which He had done. Then God blessed the seventh day and sanctified it, because in it He rested from all His work which God had created and made."

- **Exodus 20:8-11**: "Remember the Sabbath day, to keep it holy. Six days you shall labor and do all your work, but the seventh day is the Sabbath of the LORD your God. In it you shall do no work: you, nor your son, nor your daughter, nor your male servant, nor your female servant, nor your cattle, nor your stranger who is within your gates. For in six days the LORD made the heavens and the earth, the sea, and all that is in them, and rested the seventh day. Therefore the LORD blessed the Sabbath day and hallowed it."

- **Leviticus 23:3**: "Six days shall work be done, but the seventh day is a Sabbath of solemn rest, a holy convocation. You shall do no work on it; it is the Sabbath of the LORD in all your dwellings."

**God's Blessings for Keeping the Sabbath**:

> **Isaiah 56:2, 6-7** - "Blessed is the man who does this, and the son of man who lays hold on it; who keeps from defiling the Sabbath, and keeps his hand from doing any evil... Also the sons of the foreigner who join themselves to the LORD, to serve Him, and to love the name of the LORD, to be His servants—everyone who keeps from defiling the Sabbath, and holds fast My covenant—even them I will bring to My holy mountain, and make them joyful in My house of prayer... for My house shall be called a house of prayer for all nations."

> **Isaiah 58:13-14** - "If you turn away your foot from the Sabbath, from doing your pleasure on My holy day, and call the Sabbath a delight, the holy day of the LORD honorable, and shall honor Him, not doing your own ways, nor finding your own pleasure, nor speaking your own words, then you shall delight yourself in the LORD; and I will cause you to ride on the high hills of the earth, and feed you with the heritage of Jacob your father. The mouth of the LORD has spoken."

> **Ezekiel 20:12, 20** - "Moreover I also gave them My Sabbaths, to be a sign between them and Me, that they might know that I am the LORD who sanctifies them... Hallow My Sabbaths, and they will be a sign between Me and you, that you may know that I am the LORD your God."

**Key Principle**: God doesn't just command the Sabbath - He **blesses** those who keep it, promises **joy**, brings them to His **holy mountain**, and uses it as a **sign** of His sanctifying relationship with His people. The Sabbath is not a burden but a blessing, not restriction but rest, not duty but delight.

**Biblical Practice**: Saturday (7th day) - never changed in Scripture

### Currently Accepted Sabbath

**Jewish**: 
- **Saturday** (sunset Friday to sunset Saturday)
- Unchanged since biblical times

**Seventh-day Adventist & Seventh-day Baptist**:
- **Saturday** (following biblical literalism)

**Most Christians** (Catholic, Protestant, Orthodox):
- **Sunday** (1st day of the week)
- **Why the change?**
  - Resurrection of Jesus occurred on Sunday (first day)
  - Early Christians began meeting on "the Lord's Day" (Sunday)
  - Constantine made Sunday the official rest day (~321 CE)
  - Viewed as celebrating new creation, not replacing the Sabbath command

**Islamic**:
- **Friday** (Jumu'ah) - congregational prayer day, not technically a "Sabbath"

**Bottom Line**: Biblical Sabbath = **Saturday**. Christian tradition shifted observance to **Sunday** for theological and political reasons, not biblical command.

---

## Historical Timeline of Sabbath Change

### Early Period (30-150 CE)

#### Apostolic Era (30-100 CE)
- **No official change yet** - Early Christians kept Saturday Sabbath
- **Common Bible texts misused to justify Sunday observance** (and why they fail):
- **Acts 20:7** - One evening meeting on first day (Saturday night after Sabbath ended at sunset, by biblical reckoning)
  - Paul was leaving the next day, so they met late
  - This was a farewell gathering, not a regular worship service
  - Does not establish Sunday as a holy day
- **1 Corinthians 16:2** - "On the first day of the week let each one of you lay something aside, storing up as he may prosper"
  - **Context**: Paul instructing about setting aside offerings at home
  - **"Lay something aside, storing up"** = Put money away privately at home, not a church collection
  - **Why first day?**: In Roman economy, workers were commonly paid at the end of the week (after working through the Sabbath)
  - **Purpose**: So offerings would be ready when Paul arrived, not to interrupt Sabbath rest with financial matters
  - **Does NOT say**: Gather together, meet for worship, or observe Sunday as holy
  - This is about personal financial planning, not corporate worship
- **Acts 2:42, 46-47** - "They continued steadfastly in the apostles' doctrine and fellowship, in the breaking of bread... And continuing **daily** with one accord in the temple, and breaking bread from house to house"
  - **Context**: Early church growth in Jerusalem during intense evangelism period
  - **"Breaking bread daily"** = They ate meals together every day as the church grew rapidly
  - **"Daily"** = Not specific to Sunday or any particular day
  - **"From house to house"** = Informal fellowship meals, not formal worship services
  - **Does NOT specify**: Sunday as special day or replacing Sabbath
  - This passage shows daily fellowship during evangelism, not weekly Sunday worship
  - Sunday keepers cannot use this as evidence for Sunday observance since it was **daily**, not weekly
- **Key point**: Apostles continued observing **Saturday Sabbath** - no New Testament command or example of Sunday replacing it

#### Post-Apostolic (100-150 CE)
- **Gradual shift** begins among Gentile (non-Jewish) Christians
- **Epistle of Barnabas** (~130 CE) - First text arguing Sunday replaces Sabbath
- **Justin Martyr** (~150 CE) - Describes Christians worshiping on Sunday, calls it "the eighth day"

### The Major Turning Points

#### Council of Laodicea (~363-364 CE)
- **Canon 29**: Christians must not "Judaize" by resting on Saturday
- **Explicitly forbade** Saturday Sabbath observance
- **Mandated** Sunday as the Christian day of rest

#### Emperor Constantine (321 CE)
- **First civil law** making Sunday a rest day
- **Edict**: "On the venerable Day of the Sun let the magistrates and people... rest"
- Combined Christian practice with Roman "Sun day" worship
- **This is the official legal change**

#### Council of Nicaea (325 CE)
- Separated Christian practices from Jewish ones (especially Easter calculation)
- Reinforced Sunday observance

### Geographic Spread

**Where it started**:
- **Rome and Western churches** - Changed earliest (2nd-3rd century)
- **Antioch and Asia Minor** - Mixed practice longer
- **Ethiopian and some Eastern churches** - Kept both days longer
- **Abyssinian Church** - Observed both Saturday and Sunday into medieval period

### Groups That Never Changed

- **Jewish Christians** (until absorption/persecution, ~4th century)
- **Some isolated Eastern churches** (temporarily)
- **Sabbatarian movements** (emerged periodically):
  - 16th century Transylvanian Sabbatarians
  - 17th century English Sabbatarians
  - 19th century Seventh-day Adventists (1863)

### Summary Timeline

**The change happened gradually**:
- **100-200 CE**: Shift begins in Rome and Western churches (Eastern churches and other regions continued Saturday Sabbath much longer)
- **321 CE**: **Constantine's edict** - official legal change
- **325 CE**: **Council of Nicaea** - separated Christian practices from Jewish ones, reinforced Sunday
- **364 CE**: **Council of Laodicea** - ecclesiastical enforcement, banned Saturday
- **By 400 CE**: Sunday universally accepted in mainstream Christianity under Roman influence

**Important Note**: Early Christians (30-150 CE) kept the biblical Saturday Sabbath. There is no New Testament evidence of regular Sunday worship services during the apostolic period. The **official change** to Sunday was a **political and ecclesiastical decision**, not a biblical command.

---

## By Whose Authority Was the Sabbath Changed?

Based on historical evidence, the Sabbath was changed by **human ecclesiastical and political authority**, NOT by biblical or divine command.

### Authority Behind the Sabbath Change

#### 1. Emperor Constantine (321 CE) - Civil/Political Authority
- **First legal enforcement** of Sunday as rest day
- **Edict of 321 CE**: "On the venerable Day of the Sun let the magistrates and people rest"
- **Authority**: Roman Imperial law
- **Motivation**: Political unity, combining Christian practice with Roman sun worship
- **Effect**: Made Sunday observance civil law throughout the Roman Empire

#### 2. Council of Nicaea (325 CE) - Church Authority
- **Purpose**: Addressed Arian controversy, standardized Christian practices
- **Action**: Separated Christian practices from Jewish customs (especially Easter calculation)
- **Sabbath Impact**: Reinforced Sunday observance as Christian practice
- **Authority**: First Ecumenical Council of the Church
- **Effect**: Strengthened theological foundation for Sunday, distanced Christianity from Jewish Sabbath

#### 3. Council of Laodicea (363-364 CE) - Church Authority
- **Canon 29**: Explicitly forbade Saturday Sabbath, mandated Sunday
- **Authority**: Ecclesiastical council (church leadership)
- **Penalty**: Excommunication for Saturday observance
- **Effect**: Made Sunday observance official church doctrine

#### 4. Early Church Fathers (100-300 CE) - Theological Authority
- **Epistle of Barnabas** (~130 CE) - First text arguing Sunday replaces Sabbath
- **Justin Martyr** (~150 CE) - Described Sunday worship as Christian practice
- Gradually taught Sunday replaced Saturday through theological interpretation
- **Authority**: Church tradition and interpretation
- **Effect**: Laid theological groundwork for the change

**Catholic Church's Own Admission**:
The Catholic Church openly acknowledges making this change by its own authority, claiming divine power to alter God's commandments. For comprehensive documentation of this claim, see the complete collection of **[39 Official Catholic Statements](#catholic-church-sources)** in the Sources and References section, where Catholic authorities explicitly state they changed the Sabbath from Saturday to Sunday, and challenge Protestants to justify Sunday observance without accepting Catholic authority.

**Protestant Churches' Own Admission**:
Even more remarkably, Protestant theologians and denominational leaders—while claiming to follow "Bible only" (*sola scriptura*)—openly admit that Sunday observance has no biblical authority. See the complete collection of **[60 Protestant Church Statements](#protestant-churches-admissions-on-sunday-observance)** in the Sources and References section, where Protestant ministers, theologians, and church officials from Baptist, Methodist, Lutheran, Presbyterian, Anglican, Congregational, Episcopal, Church of Christ, Brethren, and other denominations explicitly acknowledge that: (1) Saturday is the biblical Sabbath, (2) No Scripture commands the change to Sunday, (3) Jesus never authorized it, (4) The apostles never ordained it, and (5) Sunday observance came from Catholic Church tradition, not biblical warrant. These admissions—now expanded to include statements from virtually every major Protestant denomination—reveal the profound inconsistency of Protestant practice: rejecting papal authority while retaining the papacy's most visible change to God's law.

### What the Bible Says About Sabbath Change

**No biblical authority exists for changing the Sabbath**:

**Old Testament Foundation**:
- **Genesis 2:2-3**: God rested on the seventh day and blessed it
- **Exodus 20:8-11**: Fourth Commandment - "Remember the Sabbath day, to keep it holy... the seventh day is the Sabbath"
- **Exodus 31:16-17**: "Perpetual covenant... a sign forever"

**Jesus's Practice**:
- **Luke 4:16**: "As his custom was, he went into the synagogue on the Sabbath day"
- **Mark 2:27-28**: "The Sabbath was made for man, and not man for the Sabbath. Therefore the Son of Man is also Lord of the Sabbath."
  - **Why Jesus is Lord of the Sabbath**: Because He created it
  - **John 1:1-3, 14**: "In the beginning was the Word, and the Word was with God, and the Word was God. He was in the beginning with God. **All things were made through Him, and without Him nothing was made that was made**... And the Word became flesh and dwelt among us."
  - **Colossians 1:16**: "For by Him all things were created that are in heaven and that are on earth, visible and invisible... All things were created through Him and for Him."
  - **Connection**: Jesus (the Word) created all things, including the Sabbath at Creation (Genesis 2:2-3)
  - **As Creator**, Jesus has authority over the Sabbath—He established it, blessed it, and sanctified it
  - **Key point**: Jesus claimed to be Lord of the Sabbath because He made it. He never claimed authority to change it or abolish it.
- Jesus never commanded changing the Sabbath day

**Jesus Rested on the Sabbath—Even in Death**:

One of the most powerful yet overlooked proofs that the Sabbath was not abolished at the cross comes from the timeline of Jesus' crucifixion, burial, and resurrection:

**The Timeline**:

**Friday (Preparation Day)**:
- **Luke 23:54** - "That day was the **Preparation**, and the Sabbath drew near."
- **Mark 15:42** - "Now when evening had come, because it was the **Preparation Day, that is, the day before the Sabbath**..."
- **John 19:31** - "Therefore, because it was the **Preparation Day**, that the bodies should not remain on the cross on the Sabbath (for that Sabbath was a high day), the Jews asked Pilate that their legs might be broken, and that they might be taken away."

**Jesus died Friday afternoon** (before sunset when Sabbath begins):
- **Matthew 27:45-50** - "Now from the sixth hour until the ninth hour there was darkness over all the land. And about the ninth hour Jesus cried out with a loud voice... And Jesus cried out again with a loud voice, and yielded up His spirit."
- **Ninth hour** = 3:00 PM (Jewish time reckoning)
- Died before sunset (when Sabbath begins at sundown)

**The Burial Was Rushed Before Sabbath**:
- **Luke 23:50-54** - "Now behold, there was a man named Joseph, a council member, a good and just man... This man went to Pilate and asked for the body of Jesus. Then he took it down, wrapped it in linen, and laid it in a tomb that was hewn out of rock, where no one had ever lain before. **That day was the Preparation, and the Sabbath drew near**."
- Joseph of Arimathea had to hurry to bury Jesus before Sabbath began at sunset
- The burial was completed just before Friday sundown

**Saturday (The Sabbath)—Jesus Rested in the Tomb**:
- **Luke 23:55-56** - "And the women who had come with Him from Galilee followed after, and they observed the tomb and how His body was laid. Then **they returned and prepared spices and fragrant oils. And they rested on the Sabbath according to the commandment**."

**Critical Point**: The women **prepared spices on Friday before sunset** and then **rested on the Sabbath according to the commandment** (Exodus 20:8-11).

**They could NOT go to the tomb on Saturday** because they were keeping the Sabbath commandment—no work allowed.

**Sunday (First Day of the Week)—The Resurrection**:
- **Mark 16:1-2** - "Now when the Sabbath was past, Mary Magdalene, Mary the mother of James, and Salome bought spices, that they might come and anoint Him. **Very early in the morning, on the first day of the week, they came to the tomb when the sun had risen**."
- **Luke 24:1** - "Now on the **first day of the week**, very early in the morning, they, and certain other women with them, came to the tomb bringing the spices which they had prepared."
- The women waited until **after the Sabbath** to go to the tomb
- They came **Sunday morning** (first day of the week) to anoint Jesus' body

**Why This Proves the Sabbath Was NOT Abolished**:

**1. If the Sabbath Was Done Away With, Why Did the Disciples Keep It After Jesus Died?**
- The disciples (including the women) kept the Sabbath **after Jesus' death**
- They rested "according to the commandment" (Luke 23:56)
- They **waited until Sunday** to go to the tomb because they couldn't work on Saturday
- If the Sabbath was abolished at the cross (Friday afternoon), they would have gone to the tomb **Saturday** to prepare Jesus' body

**2. Jesus Himself "Rested" in the Tomb on the Sabbath**:
- Died: **Friday** afternoon
- Rested in tomb: **Saturday** (the Sabbath)
- Rose: **Sunday** morning (first day of the week)
- Even in death, Jesus honored the Sabbath rest—He rested on the seventh day just as God did at Creation (Genesis 2:2-3)

**3. The Disciples Had No Knowledge of the Sabbath Changing**:
- If Jesus had abolished the Sabbath or changed it to Sunday, **the disciples didn't know about it**
- They continued keeping Saturday Sabbath immediately after His death
- They treated Saturday as holy and Sunday as a regular work day (they went to the tomb to work—anointing the body)

**4. The Argument "If the Sabbath Was Done Away With, They Could Have Gone Saturday"**:
- **The women wanted to anoint Jesus' body with spices**—this was work
- **They prepared the spices Friday** before Sabbath began
- **They rested Saturday** because the Sabbath commandment forbade work
- **They went Sunday morning** because that was the first opportunity after Sabbath ended
- If the Sabbath was abolished Friday at 3 PM (when Jesus died), **there was no reason to wait until Sunday**
- They could have gone Saturday morning—but **they didn't, because the Sabbath was still binding**

**5. Luke Wrote His Gospel 30+ Years After the Crucifixion**:
- Luke wrote his Gospel around **60-63 CE** (30+ years after Jesus' death)
- He still calls Saturday "**the Sabbath**" and Sunday "**the first day of the week**"
- He still says the women "**rested on the Sabbath according to the commandment**"
- If the Sabbath had changed to Sunday, Luke (writing decades later) would have clarified this
- Instead, he confirms: Saturday = Sabbath, Sunday = first day of the week (regular day)

**The Devastating Question for Sunday-Keepers**:

**If the Sabbath was abolished at the cross (Friday 3 PM), why did Jesus' closest followers—who were with Him for three years and witnessed His death—continue keeping Saturday Sabbath immediately after His death?**

- They knew Jesus better than anyone
- They heard all His teachings
- They witnessed His crucifixion
- Yet they **rested on Saturday** and **worked on Sunday**

**If Jesus had changed the Sabbath to Sunday or abolished it, His own disciples didn't get the memo.**

**The Pattern**:
- **Friday**: Preparation day (work to prepare for Sabbath)
- **Saturday**: Sabbath rest (no work, according to commandment)
- **Sunday**: First day of week (return to work—anointing Jesus' body)

This three-day pattern proves the Sabbath remained Saturday after the cross. The resurrection on Sunday did NOT transfer Sabbath sacredness to Sunday—the disciples still treated Sunday as a regular work day.

**Apostolic Practice**:
- **Acts 13:14**: Paul preached on the Sabbath (Saturday)
- **Acts 16:13**: Disciples met on the Sabbath
- **Acts 17:2**: Paul's custom was to attend synagogue on Sabbath
- **Acts 18:4**: "He reasoned in the synagogue every Sabbath"

**Hebrews Confirms the Sabbath Did Not Change**:
- **Hebrews 4:8-10**: "For if Joshua had given them rest, then He would not afterward have spoken of another day. There remains therefore a rest for the people of God. For he who has entered His rest has himself also ceased from his works as God did from His."
  - **Context**: Written decades after Jesus's resurrection (60s CE)
  - **"Another day"**: If God intended a different day, He would have specified it
  - **"There remains"**: Present tense - Sabbath rest still exists for God's people
  - **"As God did"**: Points back to Creation Sabbath (Genesis 2:2-3) - the seventh day
  - **Greek word "sabbatismos"** (verse 9): Literally means "Sabbath-keeping" or "Sabbath rest" - refers specifically to the seventh-day Sabbath
  - **Key point**: If the day had changed to Sunday, Hebrews would have specified this. Instead, it confirms the same Sabbath rest established at Creation remains for believers.

**New Testament Silence**:
- No verse commands changing Sabbath from Saturday to Sunday
- No apostolic decree authorizing the change
- The Fourth Commandment was never repealed or modified

**Addressing Colossians 2:16-17 - Ceremonial vs. Weekly Sabbath**:

A common objection to seventh-day Sabbath observance comes from Colossians 2:16-17. However, this passage refers to ceremonial sabbaths (annual feast days), not the weekly seventh-day Sabbath established at Creation.

> **Colossians 2:16-17** - "So let no one judge you in food or in drink, or regarding a festival or a new moon or **sabbaths**, which are a shadow of things to come, but the substance is of Christ."

**Key Biblical Distinction - Two Types of Sabbaths**:

**1. The Weekly Sabbath (Seventh Day)**:
- **Established at Creation** (Genesis 2:2-3) - before sin, before Jews, before ceremonial law
- **Written by God's finger** on stone tablets (Exodus 31:18) - part of the moral law (Ten Commandments)
- **Memorial of Creation** - points backward to God as Creator, not forward to Christ
- **"The Sabbath of the LORD"** (Exodus 20:10) - belongs to God, not ceremonial system
- **Eternal** - "A perpetual covenant... a sign forever" (Exodus 31:16-17)
- **Never called a "shadow"** - it commemorates completed creation

**2. Ceremonial Sabbaths (Annual Feast Days)**:
- **Established at Sinai** after the Exodus (Leviticus 23) - part of the ceremonial system
- **Written by Moses** in a book (Deuteronomy 31:24-26) - separate from Ten Commandments
- **Shadows pointing to Christ** - annual festivals (Passover, Day of Atonement, etc.) foreshadowed Christ's work
- **"Your sabbaths"** (Leviticus 23:32; Isaiah 1:13-14) - belonged to Israel's ceremonial system
- **Temporary** - fulfilled in Christ's sacrifice
- **Specifically called "shadows"** in Colossians 2:16-17

**Biblical Evidence for the Distinction**:

**Leviticus 23 Lists BOTH Types**:
- **Verse 3**: "Six days shall work be done, but the seventh day is a Sabbath of solemn rest" - Weekly Sabbath
- **Verses 4-44**: Annual feast sabbaths - Passover, Unleavened Bread, Pentecost, Trumpets, Day of Atonement, Tabernacles

**The weekly Sabbath is listed separately from the feast sabbaths** because it's in a different category—moral law vs. ceremonial law.

**Two Different Hebrew Terms**:
- **Weekly Sabbath**: "Shabbat" (שַׁבָּת) - singular, refers to the seventh day
- **Ceremonial Sabbaths**: "Shabbatot" (שַׁבָּתוֹת) - plural, refers to feast days that could fall on any day of the week

**Isaiah 1:13-14 Shows the Distinction**:
> "Bring no more futile sacrifices; incense is an abomination to Me. The New Moons, the Sabbaths, the calling of assemblies—I cannot endure iniquity and the sacred meeting. **Your New Moons and your appointed feasts My soul hates**; they are a trouble to Me, I am weary of bearing them."

- God calls them "**your** New Moons and **your** appointed feasts" - the ceremonial system
- He doesn't say "My Sabbath" here because He's rejecting their hypocritical observance of ceremonies
- But in Exodus 20:10, He calls the weekly Sabbath "**the Sabbath of the LORD your God**" - His Sabbath

**What Colossians 2:16-17 Actually Means**:

Paul is addressing **ceremonial regulations** that pointed forward to Christ:
- **"Food or drink"** - Ceremonial dietary laws beyond the clean/unclean distinctions (drink offerings, etc.)
- **"Festival"** - Annual feasts (Passover, Pentecost, Tabernacles)
- **"New moon"** - Monthly celebrations tied to the ceremonial calendar
- **"Sabbaths"** - Annual sabbaths associated with feast days (Day of Atonement, etc.)

**"Which are a shadow of things to come"**:
- Ceremonial sabbaths **pointed forward** to Christ's sacrifice
- The weekly Sabbath **points backward** to Creation (Exodus 20:11) - it's a memorial, not a prophecy
- Shadows end when the substance (Christ) arrives; memorials continue to commemorate what happened

**The Weekly Sabbath After the Cross**:

If the weekly Sabbath was abolished, why did:
- **Luke** call the seventh day "the Sabbath" when writing his gospel 30+ years after the cross? (Luke 23:54-56; 24:1)
- **Paul** continue keeping the Sabbath decades after the resurrection? (Acts 13:14, 42-44; 16:13; 17:2; 18:4)
- **John** refer to "the Lord's Day" (Revelation 1:10) - the same day Jesus called Himself "Lord of" (Mark 2:28)?

**Jesus Expected the Sabbath to Be Kept 40 Years After His Death (Matthew 24:15-20)**:

One of the most powerful—yet often overlooked—proofs that Jesus never abolished the Sabbath comes from His prophecy about Jerusalem's destruction:

> **Matthew 24:15-20** - "Therefore when you see the 'abomination of desolation,' spoken of by Daniel the prophet, standing in the holy place (whoever reads, let him understand), then let those who are in Judea flee to the mountains. Let him who is on the housetop not go down to take anything out of his house. And let him who is in the field not go back to get his clothes. But woe to those who are pregnant and to those who are nursing babies in those days! **And pray that your flight may not be in winter or on the Sabbath.**"

**The Prophetic Timeline**:
- **Jesus spoke these words**: ~31 CE (during His ministry)
- **Jesus was crucified**: 31 CE
- **Jerusalem was destroyed by Rome**: 70 CE (Titus's siege)
- **Time gap**: **~40 years** between Jesus's prophecy and its fulfillment

**Why This Proves the Sabbath Was Not Abolished**:

**1. Jesus Expected the Sabbath to Still Be Observed in 70 CE**:
- Jesus told His disciples to pray their flight wouldn't be on the Sabbath
- This prophecy was for events happening **40 years after His death**
- If Jesus abolished the Sabbath at the cross, why would He tell them to pray about Sabbath travel restrictions **40 years later**?

**2. The Audience Was Jews AND Gentiles**:
- By 70 CE, the church was **heavily Gentile**
- If the Sabbath was only for Jews, Jesus wouldn't have told the (future) Gentile church to pray about the Sabbath
- Yet He instructed them to pray their flight wouldn't be on the Sabbath—showing it was still binding

**3. Sabbath Travel Restrictions Would Still Apply**:
- Jesus's concern: Sabbath day's journey restrictions (Acts 1:12 - ~2,000 cubits or 0.6 miles)
- Jewish law limited travel on Sabbath to protect the day's sanctity
- Additionally, city gates would be closed on Sabbath (Nehemiah 13:19)
- Jesus expected these Sabbath restrictions to **still be in effect in 70 CE**
- Why worry about Sabbath travel limits if the Sabbath was abolished at the cross?

**4. Winter AND Sabbath—Both Practical Concerns**:
- **Winter**: Travel would be difficult due to weather
- **Sabbath**: Travel would be difficult due to religious restrictions
- Jesus lists them together as practical obstacles to fleeing
- If Sabbath was abolished, mentioning it makes no sense—it's like saying "pray your flight isn't on a day that no longer matters"

**5. This Was After the Cross**:
- Jesus spoke this **before** the crucifixion
- But He was prophesying about events **after** the crucifixion (70 CE)
- If the Sabbath ended at the cross, Jesus would have known and wouldn't have mentioned it
- Instead, He assumed the Sabbath would **still be observed 40 years later**

**The Devastating Implication for Sunday Observance**:

If Jesus:
- Expected the Sabbath to be kept in 70 CE (40 years after His death)
- Never told disciples to change the Sabbath to Sunday
- Never mentioned Sunday as a holy day
- Warned them to pray specifically about **Sabbath** travel restrictions

**Then how can Christians claim**:
- Jesus abolished the Sabbath at the cross?
- The resurrection changed the day to Sunday?
- The Sabbath was only for Jews?

**Jesus's own words prove He expected the seventh-day Sabbath to continue being observed by His followers decades after His death and resurrection.**

**Historical Fulfillment**:

When Jerusalem was destroyed in 70 CE:
- Early Christians (following Jesus's warning) fled to Pella before the siege
- They heeded Jesus's prophecy and escaped
- **The Sabbath was still being observed** by the Christian community
- Jesus's warning about the Sabbath was fulfilled—it **was** still in effect 40 years after the cross

**The Question That Cannot Be Avoided**:

**If Jesus abolished the Sabbath, why did He tell His disciples to pray that their escape from Jerusalem—40 years after His death—wouldn't be on the Sabbath?**

This single verse dismantles the entire argument that:
- The Sabbath ended at the cross
- Sunday replaced Saturday after the resurrection
- The Sabbath was only for Jews
- The law was abolished

**Jesus Himself expected the Sabbath to be kept by His followers in 70 CE. That's 40 years after the cross, 40 years after the supposed "abolishment" of the law, 40 years into the "New Covenant" era.**

**The Sabbath was not abolished. Jesus expected it to continue. His disciples kept it. The early church observed it. Only later did human tradition change it to Sunday.**

**Hebrews 4:9 Confirms the Sabbath Remains**:
> "There remains therefore a **Sabbath rest** [Greek: sabbatismos] for the people of God."

The Greek word **sabbatismos** literally means "Sabbath-keeping" or "observance of the Sabbath." If the Sabbath was abolished, Hebrews (written after the cross) wouldn't say it "remains" for God's people.

**The Bottom Line**:

Colossians 2:16-17 addresses **ceremonial sabbaths** that were shadows of Christ's atoning work. The **weekly seventh-day Sabbath**:
- Was established at Creation (before sin)
- Is part of the Ten Commandments (moral law)
- Points backward to God as Creator (memorial)
- Was never called a "shadow"
- Continued to be observed by apostles after the cross
- Remains for God's people (Hebrews 4:9)

**The Critical Distinction - Two Laws, Two Locations**:

**The ceremonial system ended at the cross** (Colossians 2:14 - "having wiped out the handwriting of requirements that was against us"). But **the weekly Sabbath predates the ceremonial system** and continues as God's holy day, His sign of Creation and sanctification.

Understanding what ended at the cross requires recognizing the biblical distinction between **two separate laws**:

**1. God's Law (The Ten Commandments - Moral Law)**:
- **Written by God's own finger** on stone tablets (Exodus 31:18; Deuteronomy 9:10)
  > "And He gave Moses two tablets of the Testimony, tablets of stone, **written with the finger of God**." (Exodus 31:18)
- **Placed INSIDE the Ark of the Covenant** (Exodus 25:16, 21; Deuteronomy 10:5)
  > "And you shall put **into the ark** the Testimony which I will give you." (Exodus 25:16)
- **Not a witness AGAINST us** - God's perfect standard of righteousness
- **Eternal and unchangeable** - "All His precepts are sure. They stand fast forever and ever" (Psalm 111:7-8)
- **Includes the weekly Sabbath** - the fourth commandment (Exodus 20:8-11)

**2. Moses' Law (The Ceremonial Law)**:
- **Written by Moses** in a book (Deuteronomy 31:9, 24)
  > "So Moses wrote this law and delivered it to the priests... So it was, **when Moses had completed writing the words of this law in a book**, when they were finished..." (Deuteronomy 31:9, 24)
- **Placed BESIDE (outside) the Ark** as a witness against Israel (Deuteronomy 31:26)
  > "Take this Book of the Law, and put it **beside the ark** of the covenant of the LORD your God, that it may be there **as a witness against you**." (Deuteronomy 31:26)
- **A witness AGAINST Israel** - contained penalties for breaking God's law, animal sacrifices for sin
- **Temporary** - "shadows of things to come" (Colossians 2:17), fulfilled in Christ
- **Includes ceremonial sabbaths** - annual feast days that pointed to Christ (Leviticus 23:4-44)

**What Colossians 2:14 Actually Says**:

> **Colossians 2:14** - "Having wiped out **the handwriting of requirements** that was against us, which was contrary to us. And He has taken it out of the way, having nailed it to the cross."

**"The handwriting of requirements"** (Greek: *cheirographon tois dogmasin*) = The written document of ordinances

**Key Points**:
- **"Handwriting"** - Written by human hand (Moses), not God's finger
- **"Requirements"** - Ceremonial ordinances, regulations, rituals
- **"Against us"** - The law placed **beside the ark as a witness against Israel** (Deuteronomy 31:26)
- **"Contrary to us"** - Contained penalties and sacrifices required because of our sin

**This describes Moses' ceremonial law**, not the Ten Commandments:
- God's law (Ten Commandments) was **written by God's finger**, not by hand
- God's law was placed **inside the ark**, not beside it as a witness against us
- God's law is **eternal**, not temporary ordinances

**The Ten Commandments Were Never "Against Us"**:

God's moral law defines righteousness and reveals sin, but it's not "against us" in the sense of being abolished:
- **Romans 7:12** - "Therefore the law is **holy**, and the commandment holy and just and good."
- **Romans 3:31** - "Do we then make void the law through faith? Certainly not! On the contrary, **we establish the law**."
- **1 John 5:3** - "For this is the love of God, that we keep His commandments. And **His commandments are not burdensome**."

The ceremonial law was "against us" because it testified to our guilt and prescribed endless animal sacrifices—a constant reminder of sin. **This** is what was nailed to the cross, not God's eternal moral law.

**Summary - What Ended vs. What Continues**:

| **Aspect** | **Moses' Ceremonial Law** | **God's Moral Law (Ten Commandments)** |
|-----------|--------------------------|--------------------------------------|
| **Written by** | Moses (human hand) | God's finger |
| **Written on** | Book/scroll | Stone tablets |
| **Placed** | **Beside** the ark | **Inside** the ark |
| **Purpose** | Witness **against** Israel | Standard of righteousness |
| **Nature** | Temporary shadows | Eternal principles |
| **Status** | Ended at the cross | Continues forever |
| **Sabbaths** | Ceremonial (annual feasts) | Weekly seventh-day Sabbath |

**The weekly Sabbath was established at Creation (Genesis 2:2-3), written by God's finger in the Ten Commandments (Exodus 31:18), placed inside the ark (Exodus 25:16), and continues as God's holy day—His sign of Creation and sanctification (Ezekiel 20:12, 20).**

---

## Addressing the "Sabbath Was Only for Israel" Objection

One of the most frequently raised objections to Sabbath observance is the claim: *"The Sabbath was a Jewish institution given specifically to the nation of Israel at Mount Sinai—it was never intended for Gentiles or for all of humanity."*

This objection collapses when we examine three categories of biblical evidence that place the Sabbath—and God's entire moral law—firmly **before** Abraham, **before** the Exodus, **before** Mount Sinai, and **before** Israel ever existed as a nation.

---

### Proof 1: The Manna Miracle (Exodus 16) — Sabbath Enforced Before Israel Was a Nation

**The Timeline Is Critical**

The book of Exodus records two pivotal events in sequence:
- **Exodus 16**: The manna in the wilderness — *in the wilderness of Sin*
- **Exodus 19-20**: Israel arrives at Mount Sinai and receives the Ten Commandments

The manna episode in Exodus 16 occurs **weeks before Sinai**. The people were not yet an established covenant nation. They had no Mosaic law. No tablets had been given. No national covenant had been ratified.

Yet notice what God does:

> **Exodus 16:4** — "Then the LORD said to Moses, 'Behold, I will rain bread from heaven for you. And the people shall go out and gather a certain quota every day, that **I may test them, whether they will walk in My law or not.**'"

God explicitly states He is using the manna to test whether they will walk in **"My law"** — a law that already existed before Sinai. He does not say "a law I am about to give them." The law is already His, already pre-existing.

**The Sabbath Instruction Before the Commandment Was Formally Given**:

> **Exodus 16:22-26** — "And so it was, on the sixth day, that they gathered **twice as much bread**... And he said to them, 'This is what the LORD has said: "Tomorrow is a Sabbath rest, a holy Sabbath to the LORD. Bake what you will bake today... for tomorrow is a Sabbath to the LORD."'"

God instructs them concerning the Sabbath—gathering double on the sixth day, resting on the seventh—**before** the Ten Commandments were given at Sinai. The Sabbath is presented not as something new, but as an existing, recognized institution.

**The Rebuke That Reveals Everything**:

> **Exodus 16:27-28** — "Now it happened that some of the people went out on the seventh day to gather, but they found none. And the LORD said to Moses, **'How long do you refuse to keep My commandments and My laws?'**"

This rebuke is devastating to the "Sabbath only for Israel at Sinai" argument. Consider:

- **"How long"** — This phrase implies ongoing, repeated refusal, not a first-time violation of a newly introduced rule
- **"My commandments and My laws"** — God uses the plural, referring to an established body of law, not a single new ordinance being introduced
- God held them **accountable** for breaking the Sabbath **before** the Sinai covenant was ratified
- If the Sabbath were a new institution being introduced at this moment, God's question "how long do you refuse?" would make no logical sense

**The Conclusion**: God treated the Sabbath as a known, pre-existing obligation — binding on a disorganized group of former slaves who had not yet arrived at Sinai and had not yet been formally constituted as a covenant nation.

---

### Proof 2: Nehemiah 9:14 — The Sabbath Was "Made Known," Implying Prior Existence

> **Nehemiah 9:14** — "You **made known** to them Your holy Sabbath, and commanded them precepts, statutes and laws, by the hand of Moses Your servant."

**The Language of Prior Existence**

The Hebrew verb used here — **הוֹדַעְתָּ** (*hoda'ta*, "You made known") — carries a critical implication. One cannot "make known" something that did not previously exist. You reveal, remind, and re-proclaim what already exists but has been forgotten or obscured.

Consider the parallel usage:
> **Psalm 103:7** — "He **made known** His ways to Moses, His acts to the children of Israel."

God's *ways* did not begin with Moses — God simply revealed them to Moses. In the same way, the Sabbath was not born at Sinai — it was **re-proclaimed** to a people who had lost track of it.

**The 400-Year Gap — Why They Needed It "Made Known"**

The context of Nehemiah 9 is a sweeping historical prayer that begins at Creation and traces Israel's journey. The answer to *why* the Sabbath needed to be "made known" lies in Israel's immediate history:

- The descendants of Jacob entered Egypt ~1876 BC
- They remained in Egypt for approximately **400 years** (Genesis 15:13; Acts 7:6)
- During 400 years of slavery under Egyptian masters, they could not freely observe a weekly rest
- Egyptian religious culture was built around the sun calendar and polytheistic ritual, not a seventh-day Sabbath
- By the time of the Exodus, the people had been immersed in Egyptian culture for four centuries — the Sabbath had been forgotten in practice

When God "made known" the Sabbath through Moses, He was **restoring** to His people a Creation ordinance they had lost — not inventing a new Jewish institution.

**The Implication**: If the Sabbath had been exclusively a Mosaic institution invented at Sinai for Israel, Nehemiah's prayer would logically read "You *gave them* Your holy Sabbath" — introducing something new. Instead, the language of "making known" confirms the Sabbath pre-existed the nation of Israel entirely.

---

### Proof 3: Cain and Abel (Genesis 4) — The Full Moral Law Pre-Existed the Nation of Israel

**The Argument from Accountability**

> **Genesis 4:8-12** — "Now Cain talked with Abel his brother; and it came to pass, when they were in the field, that Cain rose up against Abel his brother and **killed him**. So the LORD said to Cain, 'Where is Abel your brother?' He said, 'I do not know. Am I my brother's keeper?' And He said, 'What have you done? The voice of your brother's blood cries out to Me from the ground. So now **you are cursed** from the earth...'"

God holds Cain fully accountable for the murder of Abel — pronouncing a specific curse and judgment upon him. Yet this occurred:

- Long before Abraham (Genesis 12, ~2000 BC)
- Long before Moses or the Exodus (~1450 BC)
- Long before Mount Sinai and the formal giving of the Ten Commandments
- Long before Israel existed in any form as a people or nation

**The Biblical Logic of Law and Accountability**

Scripture provides an airtight logical framework:

> **1 John 3:4** — "Whoever commits sin also commits lawlessness, for **sin is the transgression of the law**."

> **Romans 4:15** — "For the law brings about wrath; for **where there is no law there is no transgression**."

> **Romans 5:13** — "For until the law sin was in the world, but **sin is not imputed where there is no law**."

The chain of reasoning is clear:
1. Sin = transgression of the law
2. Where there is no law, there is no transgression
3. Therefore: if God holds someone accountable for sin, a law must exist

**God held Cain accountable for murder. Therefore the law against murder existed when Cain killed Abel.** The sixth commandment — "You shall not murder" (Exodus 20:13) — was binding on Cain, a man who lived thousands of years before Sinai, before Israel, before Moses, before Abraham.

**The Principle of Indivisibility of the Moral Law**

The critical implication for the Sabbath objection is this: **You cannot selectively apply the Ten Commandments.**

If the sixth commandment (Do not murder) was binding on all humanity before Sinai, then all ten commandments were binding on all humanity before Sinai — including the **fourth commandment**: *"Remember the Sabbath day, to keep it holy."*

The Ten Commandments are not a buffet from which we select the commands we find convenient. They form a unified moral code that Scripture treats as indivisible:

> **James 2:10-11** — "For whoever shall keep the whole law, and yet stumble in one point, he is guilty of all. For He who said, 'Do not commit adultery,' also said, 'Do not murder.' If you do not commit adultery, but you do murder, you have become a transgressor of the law."

James affirms the unity of the law — breaking any single commandment implicates the whole law. If the sixth commandment applied to Cain, the fourth did too.

**Additional Pre-Sinai Law Evidence**:

The Cain and Abel account is not isolated. Scripture records moral accountability before Sinai throughout Genesis:

| **Event** | **Reference** | **Law Implied** |
|-----------|--------------|----------------|
| Cain murders Abel — God judges | Genesis 4:8-12 | 6th Commandment (Do not murder) |
| God judges the world in the Flood for wickedness | Genesis 6:5-7 | Moral law violated universally |
| Sodom and Gomorrah destroyed for sin | Genesis 19 | Moral law binding on all nations |
| Joseph refuses Potiphar's wife: "sin against God" | Genesis 39:9 | 7th Commandment (Do not commit adultery) |
| Abraham obeys God's "commandments, statutes, and laws" | Genesis 26:5 | Full moral law pre-Sinai |

> **Genesis 26:5** — "Because Abraham obeyed My voice and kept My charge, My commandments, **My statutes, and My laws**."

God tells Isaac that Abraham kept His "commandments, statutes, and laws" — the identical terminology used for the full Mosaic law — *centuries before Moses was born*.

---

### The Three Proofs United — One Unbreakable Conclusion

All three lines of evidence converge on a single historical and theological reality:

| **Evidence** | **When** | **What It Proves** |
|-------------|----------|-------------------|
| **Cain and Abel** (Genesis 4) | Before any nation | Moral law (incl. 6th Commandment) binding on all humanity |
| **Nehemiah 9:14** | Exodus period | Sabbath "made known" — implies prior existence before Sinai |
| **Exodus 16 Manna** | Before Sinai | Sabbath enforced weeks before the Ten Commandments given; God rebukes "how long" |

The Sabbath was binding and recognized:
- ✅ **Before Abraham** — the fall of Cain
- ✅ **Before the Exodus** — Nehemiah confirms it existed before Moses "made it known"
- ✅ **Before Sinai** — Exodus 16 occurs weeks before the giving of the law, yet God enforces the Sabbath and rebukes its violation

**The "Sabbath Only for Israel" argument fails at every pre-Sinai test point.** The Sabbath is not a national Jewish ordinance—it is a **Creation ordinance for all of humanity**, established on the seventh day of the first week of earth's existence (Genesis 2:2-3), long before any nation, covenant, or ethnicity existed.

**Jesus Himself Settled the Question**:

> **Mark 2:27** — "The Sabbath was made **for man**, not man for the Sabbath."

The Greek word Jesus uses is **ἄνθρωπος** (*anthropos*) — the generic word for *human being*, *mankind*, *humanity*. He did not say "for Israel," "for Jews," or "for the covenant people." He said the Sabbath was made for **man** — the entire human race.

And He said it was *"made"* (past tense, already established) — pointing back to Creation, when God "made" the Sabbath (Genesis 2:2-3), **2,000 years before Israel existed as a nation.**

> **Isaiah 56:2, 6-7** — "Blessed is the man who does this... who keeps from defiling the Sabbath... **Also the sons of the foreigner** who join themselves to the LORD, to serve Him, and to love the name of the LORD, to be His servants—**everyone who keeps from defiling the Sabbath**... even them I will bring to My holy mountain, and make them joyful in My house of prayer. **For My house shall be called a house of prayer for all nations.**"

God specifically extends the Sabbath blessing to **foreigners** — non-Israelites — who join themselves to the LORD. If the Sabbath were exclusively for Israel, this invitation would be meaningless. Instead, God frames Sabbath observance as the identifying mark of *all* who love and follow Him, **from every nation on earth**.

---

**Addressing Romans 14:5 - Context is Key**:

Another commonly misused verse to justify Sunday observance or disregarding the Sabbath is Romans 14:5. However, when read in full context, this passage has nothing to do with the weekly Sabbath—it concerns personal fasting practices and food controversies in the early church.

> **Romans 14:5-6** - "One person esteems one day above another; another esteems every day alike. Let each be fully convinced in his own mind. He who observes the day, observes it to the Lord; and he who does not observe the day, to the Lord he does not observe it. He who eats, eats to the Lord, for he gives God thanks; and he who does not eat, to the Lord he does not eat, and gives God thanks."

**Reading in Full Context (Romans 14:1-23)**:

**The Chapter's Theme - Food and Voluntary Fasting Days**:

> **Romans 14:1-3** - "Receive one who is weak in the faith, but not to disputes over doubtful matters. For one believes he may **eat all things**, but he who is weak **eats only vegetables**. Let not him who eats despise him who does not eat, and let not him who does not eat judge him who eats; for God has received him."

- **Context**: Dispute over **food** - some ate meat, others only vegetables
- **"Doubtful matters"** (Greek: *dialogismōn*) - debatable issues, not God's commandments
- **Key question**: Were the Ten Commandments ever called "doubtful matters"? No.

> **Romans 14:5-6** - "One person esteems one day above another; another esteems every day alike... He who observes the day, observes it to the Lord... **He who eats, eats to the Lord**; for he gives God thanks; **and he who does not eat**, to the Lord he does not eat, and gives God thanks."

- **"The day"** - Connected directly to eating and not eating
- **Context**: Voluntary fasting days, not the weekly Sabbath
- Jewish believers observed additional fast days; Gentile believers did not
- Both were acceptable as long as done "to the Lord"

> **Romans 14:17** - "For the kingdom of God is not **eating and drinking**, but righteousness and peace and joy in the Holy Spirit."

- Paul summarizes: The controversy is about **eating and drinking**, not Sabbath observance
- The weekly Sabbath command says nothing about fasting or food choices

> **Romans 14:20-21** - "Do not destroy the work of God for the sake of **food**. All things indeed are pure, but it is evil for the man who eats with offense. It is good neither to **eat meat nor drink wine** nor do anything by which your brother stumbles or is offended or is made weak."

- Final verses confirm: The entire chapter concerns **food and drink**, not the Sabbath

**Why Romans 14:5 Cannot Refer to the Weekly Sabbath**:

**1. The Context is Food, Not Worship Days**:
- Romans 14 mentions "eating" or "food" **15 times**
- It mentions "the Sabbath" **0 times**
- Paul explicitly states the issue: "eating and drinking" (verse 17), "food" (verse 20), "eat meat nor drink wine" (verse 21)

**2. The Weekly Sabbath is Not a "Doubtful Matter"**:
- Verse 1 calls these "doubtful matters" (debatable issues)
- The Sabbath commandment was written by God's finger on stone (Exodus 31:18)
- God never called His Sabbath a "doubtful matter"—He called it "holy" (Exodus 20:8)

**3. Paul Continued Keeping the Sabbath**:
- **Acts 17:2** - "Then Paul, **as his custom was**, went in to them, and for three Sabbaths reasoned with them from the Scriptures."
- **Acts 18:4** - "And he reasoned in the synagogue **every Sabbath**, and persuaded both Jews and Greeks."
- If Paul taught Romans 14:5 meant the Sabbath was optional, why did he continue observing it as his custom?

**4. The Weekly Sabbath is "To the Lord"**:
- Romans 14:6 says whatever day is observed should be "to the Lord"
- Exodus 20:10 calls the Sabbath "**the Sabbath of the LORD your God**"—it already belongs to the Lord
- God established which day is "to the Lord" at Creation—humans don't choose

**5. Paul Says "Do All for the Glory of God"**:
> **Romans 14:23** - "But he who doubts is condemned if he eats, because he does not eat from faith; for **whatever is not from faith is sin**."

> **1 Corinthians 10:31** - "Therefore, whether you **eat or drink**, or whatever you do, **do all to the glory of God**."

- Paul's conclusion: Do everything (including food choices) for God's glory
- How do we glorify God? By obeying His commandments: "Remember the Sabbath day, to keep it holy" (Exodus 20:8)
- We cannot "glorify God" by disobeying His explicit command

**What Romans 14 Actually Addresses**:

Paul is addressing **voluntary religious practices** regarding food and personal fasting days:
- Some Jewish believers observed additional fast days beyond what God commanded
- Some abstained from meat (possibly offered to idols) or wine
- These were **human traditions**, not divine commands
- Paul says: Don't judge each other over these non-essential practices

**Romans 14 does NOT address**:
- The weekly seventh-day Sabbath (never mentioned)
- God's Ten Commandments (called "doubtful matters" would be blasphemous)
- Replacing Saturday Sabbath with Sunday (no biblical warrant)

**The Sabbath vs. Human Traditions**:

| **God's Sabbath (Exodus 20:8-11)** | **Human Fasting Days (Romans 14)** |
|-----------------------------------|-----------------------------------|
| Commanded by God | Voluntary human tradition |
| Written by God's finger on stone | Not written by God |
| Fourth Commandment | "Doubtful matter" |
| Specific day: Seventh day | Any day chosen by individual |
| Not about food | Specifically about food/fasting |
| "The Sabbath of the LORD" | Personal choice "to the Lord" |

**Conclusion**:

Romans 14:5 addresses **voluntary fasting days and food controversies**—matters of personal conscience where God gave no specific command. The **weekly Sabbath** is not a "doubtful matter" or personal preference—it is the fourth commandment, written by God's finger, established at Creation, and observed by Jesus, the apostles, and the early church.

Using Romans 14:5 to justify Sunday observance or discarding the Sabbath is taking Scripture out of context. Paul's message is: Don't argue over non-essential food customs and voluntary fast days. But God's command to "Remember the Sabbath day, to keep it holy" (Exodus 20:8) is not optional, negotiable, or subject to personal preference.

### What Authority Was Used?

| Authority | Type | Date | Action |
|-----------|------|------|--------|
| **Constantine** | Roman Emperor (Political) | 321 CE | Made Sunday rest day civil law |
| **Council of Nicaea** | Church Council (Ecclesiastical) | 325 CE | Reinforced Sunday, separated from Jewish practices |
| **Council of Laodicea** | Church Council (Ecclesiastical) | 364 CE | Made Sunday church law, banned Saturday |
| **Church Fathers** | Theological Leaders | 100-300 CE | Taught Sunday replaces Saturday |
| **Church Tradition** | Human Interpretation | 2nd-4th century | Gradual shift in practice |

**The change was authorized by:**
- ✓ Political/Imperial power (Constantine)
- ✓ Ecclesiastical/Church power (Councils)
- ✓ Human tradition (Church Fathers)
- ✓ Theological interpretation (non-biblical)

**The change was NOT authorized by:**
- ✗ Jesus Christ
- ✗ The Apostles
- ✗ Biblical command
- ✗ Divine revelation
- ✗ Scriptural authority

### Critical Question

**Can human authority (political or ecclesiastical) change what God commanded?**

The biblical position is clear:

**Obeying God Rather Than Men**:
- **Acts 5:29**: "Then Peter and the other apostles answered and said: 'We ought to obey God rather than men.'"

**Human Tradition vs. God's Commandments**:
- **Mark 7:6-9**: "He answered and said to them, 'Well did Isaiah prophesy of you hypocrites, as it is written: "This people honors Me with their lips, but their heart is far from Me. And in vain they worship Me, teaching as doctrines the commandments of men." For laying aside the commandment of God, you hold the tradition of men.' He said to them, 'All too well you reject the commandment of God, that you may keep your tradition.'"

- **Mark 7:13**: "Making the word of God of no effect through your tradition which you have handed down. And many such things you do."

- **Matthew 15:3**: "He answered and said to them, 'Why do you also transgress the commandment of God because of your tradition?'"

- **Matthew 15:6**: "Thus you have made the commandment of God of no effect by your tradition."

- **Matthew 15:9**: "And in vain they worship Me, teaching as doctrines the commandments of men."
