### Catholic Church Sources

**Official Catholic Statements on Sunday Change**:

1. **The Catholic Mirror** (Official Organ of Cardinal Gibbons):
   - *"The Christian Sabbath, the Genuine Offspring of the Union of the Holy Spirit with the Catholic Church His Spouse"* - Series of articles, September 1893
   - **Key Quote**: "The Catholic Church, for over one thousand years before the existence of a Protestant, by virtue of her divine mission, changed the day from Saturday to Sunday... The Christian Sabbath is therefore to this day the acknowledged offspring of the Catholic Church as spouse of the Holy Ghost, without a word of remonstrance from the Protestant world."
   - **Significance**: Official Catholic publication explicitly claiming sole authority for Sabbath change

2. **Rome's Challenge: Why Do Protestants Keep Sunday?**:
   - Published by Catholic church sources (various editions, early-to-mid 1900s)
   - **Core Argument**: Challenges Protestants to justify Sunday observance when the Bible commands Saturday Sabbath
   - **Key Quote**: "The [Catholic] Church changed the observance of the Sabbath to Sunday by right of the divine, infallible authority given to her by her founder, Jesus Christ. The Protestant claiming the Bible to be the only guide of faith, has no warrant for observing Sunday."
   - **Significance**: Catholic Church openly challenges biblical authority of Sunday, claims only Catholic tradition supports it

3. **The Christian Sabbath** (Catholic Educational Literature):
   - Various Catholic publications explaining Sunday as "Christian Sabbath"
   - **Argument**: Church authority supersedes biblical commandment
   - **Position**: Catholics consistently acknowledge no biblical basis for Sunday, claim church authority alone made the change

4. **The Convert's Catechism of Catholic Doctrine** (Rev. Peter Geiermann, C.SS.R.):
   - Published 1910, approved by Catholic Church authorities
   - **Question and Answer Format**:
     - **Q**: "Which is the Sabbath day?"
     - **A**: "Saturday is the Sabbath day."
     - **Q**: "Why do we observe Sunday instead of Saturday?"
     - **A**: "We observe Sunday instead of Saturday because the Catholic Church, in the Council of Laodicea (A.D. 336), transferred the solemnity from Saturday to Sunday."
   - **Note**: The catechism incorrectly dates the Council of Laodicea to 336 CE; the actual date was approximately 363-364 CE. This historical error in the Catholic source does not change the admission that the Church, not Scripture, changed the Sabbath.
   - **Key Quote**: "The Church substituted Sunday for Saturday by the plenitude of that divine power which Jesus Christ bestowed upon her."
   - **Significance**: Official Catholic catechism for converts explicitly teaches that Saturday is the biblical Sabbath, but the Church changed it to Sunday by its own authority

5. **The Question Box: Answers to Questions Received on Missions to Non-Catholics**:
   - Catholic missionary handbook used for evangelism and answering Protestant objections
   - Published by Paulist Fathers (various editions throughout 20th century)
   - **On the Sabbath Question**:
     - Acknowledges the biblical Sabbath is Saturday
     - States Catholics transferred observance to Sunday by church authority
     - Presents the change as proof of Catholic Church's divine authority
   - **Key Argument**: "If Protestants follow the Bible only, they should observe Saturday; by keeping Sunday they acknowledge Catholic Church authority."
   - **Significance**: Used as evangelistic tool showing that Sunday observance proves Catholic Church has authority to change God's commandments - turns Protestant inconsistency into Catholic apologetic

6. **Saint Catherine Catholic Church Sentinel**, May 21, 1995 (Pastor's Page):
   - **Quote**: "Perhaps the boldest thing, the most revolutionary change the Church ever did, happened in the first century. The holy day, the Sabbath, was changed from Saturday to Sunday... not from any directions noted in the Scriptures, but from the Church's sense of its own power... People who think that the Scriptures should be the sole authority, should logically become 7th Day Adventists, and keep Saturday holy."
   - **Significance**: Modern (1995) Catholic parish publication explicitly stating the Church changed the Sabbath "not from any directions noted in the Scriptures, but from the Church's sense of its own power" - remarkable candor that the change had no biblical basis and was based solely on claimed church authority

7. **The Australian Catholic Truth Society Record**, February 10, 1950:
   - **Statement**: "Sunday is a Catholic institution and its claim to observance can be defended only on Catholic principles... From beginning to end of Scripture there is not a single passage that warrants the transfer of weekly public worship from the last day of the week to the first."
   - **Significance**: Official Catholic Truth Society publication acknowledging no scriptural warrant for Sunday observance, that it is purely a Catholic institution defended only by church authority

8. **The Catholic Universe Bulletin**, August 14, 1942:
   - **Quote**: "The Church changed the observance of the Sabbath to Sunday by right of the divine, infallible authority given to her by her Founder, Jesus Christ."
   - **Significance**: 20th century reaffirmation of church's claim to change God's law

9. **Catholic Catechism** (Current edition):
   - Ten Commandments listing with second commandment removed, tenth split
   - Sunday observance teaching replacing biblical Sabbath
   - Official doctrinal position of Catholic Church

10. **Papal Encyclicals on Sunday Observance**:
   - *Dies Domini* (Apostolic Letter on the Lord's Day) by Pope John Paul II, 1998
   - Various papal statements affirming Sunday as "the Lord's Day"

**Vatican Documents**:
- Lateran Treaty (1929) - Re-establishment of Vatican City as sovereign state
- Concordats with various nations
- Vatican diplomatic correspondence

**Additional Catholic Doctrinal and Apologetic Sources**:

11. **Canon Cafferata, The Catechism Explained**, p. 89:
   - Standard Catholic catechism explanation
   - **Quote**: "The Church substituted Sunday for Saturday by the plenitude of the divine power which she received from her Founder, Jesus Christ."
   - **Significance**: Acknowledges Church authority superseded biblical Sabbath command

12. **Catholic Press**, August 25, 1900:
   - Early 20th-century Catholic periodical
   - **Quote**: "Sunday is a Catholic institution, and... can be defended only on Catholic principles... From beginning to end of Scripture there is not a single passage that warrants the transfer of weekly public worship from the last day of the week to the first."
   - **Significance**: Explicitly states no biblical basis for Sunday

13. **Rev. John Laux, M.A., A Course in Religion for Catholic High Schools and Academies**:
   - Benzinger Brothers, 1936 edition, Part 1, p. 51
   - **Quote**: "Some theologians have held that God likewise directly determined the Sunday as the day of worship in the New Law, that He Himself has explicitly substituted the Sunday for the Sabbath. But this theory is now entirely abandoned. It is now commonly held that God simply gave His Church the power to set aside whatever day or days she would deem suitable as Holy Days. The Church chose Sunday, the first day of the week, and in the course of time added other days as holy days."
   - **Significance**: Catholic educational textbook used to instruct youth, explicitly teaching Church chose Sunday by its own power, not biblical command

14. **Vincent J. Kelly, Forbidden Sunday and Feast-Day Occupations**:
   - Washington, DC: Catholic University of America Press, 1943
   - Studies in Sacred Theology, No. 70, p. 2
   - **Quote**: "The Sabbath was Saturday, not Sunday... The early Christians did not transfer the observance of the seventh day to the first. On the contrary, they added the observance of the first day... It was not until several hundred years after Christ that the Sabbath observance was by law transferred from Saturday to Sunday."
   - **Significance**: Academic theological work acknowledging change happened centuries after Christ, not by apostolic authority

15. **Henry Tuberville, An Abridgment of the Christian Doctrine** (1833 approbation):
   - Page 58 (Same statement in *Manual of Christian Doctrine*, ed. by Daniel Ferris [1916 ed.], p. 67)
   - **Q**: "Have you any other way of proving that the Church has power to institute festivals of precept?"
   - **A**: "Had she not such power, she could not have done that in which all modern religionists agree with her—she could not have substituted the observance of Sunday, the first day of the week, for the observance of Saturday, the seventh day, a change for which there is no Scriptural authority."
   - **Significance**: Long-standing Catholic teaching (1833-1916) using Sunday change as proof of Church authority

16. **Our Sunday Visitor**, October 7, 1951:
   - Major Catholic weekly newspaper
   - **Quote**: "Not the Creator of the Universe in Genesis 2:1-3, but the Catholic Church can claim the honor of having granted man a pause to his work every seven days."
   - **Significance**: Claims Catholic Church, not God, granted the weekly rest day

17. **William Gildea, Doctor of Divinity, The Catholic World**, March 1894, p. 809:
   - Catholic intellectual journal
   - **Quote**: "We hold upon this earth the place of God Almighty... The Pope is of so great dignity and so exalted that he is not a mere man, but as it were God, and the vicar of God."
   - **Significance**: Scholarly defense of papal authority to change God's laws

18. **Lucius Ferraris, Prompta Bibliotheca**, art. Papa, II, Vol. VI, p. 29:
   - Encyclopedic work on papal authority
   - **Quote**: "The Pope is of so great authority and power that he can modify, explain, or interpret even divine laws... The Pope can modify divine law, since his power is not of man but of God, and he acts as vicegerent of God upon earth."
   - **Significance**: Claims Pope has power to change divine law itself

19. **Adrien Nampon, Catholic Doctrine as Defined by the Council of Trent**, p. 157:
   - Explanation of official Catholic teaching from Council of Trent
   - **Quote**: "The Scriptures alone do not contain all the truths which a Christian is bound to believe, nor do they explicitly enjoin all the duties which he is obliged to practice. Not to mention other examples, is not every Christian obliged to sanctify Sunday and to abstain on that day from unnecessary servile work? Is not the observance of this law among the most prominent of our sacred duties? But you may read the Bible from Genesis to Revelation, and you will not find a single line authorizing the sanctification of Sunday. The Scriptures enforce the religious observance of Saturday, a day which we never sanctify."
   - **Significance**: Council of Trent doctrine acknowledging no biblical basis for Sunday, claiming tradition supersedes Scripture

20. **C. F. Thomas, Chancellor of Cardinal Gibbons**, letter dated November 11, 1895:
   - Official response to inquiry about Sabbath change
   - **Quote**: "Of course the Catholic Church claims that the change was her act... And the act is a MARK of her ecclesiastical power and authority in religious matters."
   - **Significance**: High-ranking Church official explicitly stating Sunday change is the "MARK" of Catholic authority

21. **T. Enright, C.S.S.R., lecture delivered in 1893**:
   - Catholic priest's public defense of Church's power to change Sabbath
   - **Quote**: "I have repeatedly offered $1,000 to anyone who can prove to me from the Bible alone that I am bound to keep Sunday holy. There is no such law in the Bible. It is a law of the holy Catholic Church alone. The Bible says, 'Remember the Sabbath day to keep it holy.' The Catholic Church says: 'No. By my divine power I abolish the Sabbath day and command you to keep holy the first day of the week.' And lo! The entire civilized world bows down in a reverent obedience to the command of the holy Catholic Church."
   - **Significance**: Public challenge offering $1,000 for biblical proof of Sunday, admitting entire practice rests on Catholic authority alone

22. **Library of Christian Doctrine: Why Don't You Keep Holy the Sabbath-Day?**:
   - London: Burns and Oates, Ltd., pp. 3, 4
   - **Quote**: "You will tell me that Saturday was the Jewish Sabbath, but that the Christian Sabbath has been changed to Sunday. Changed! but by whom? Who has authority to change an express commandment of Almighty God? When God has spoken and said, Thou shalt keep holy the seventh day, who shall dare to say, Nay, thou mayest work and do all manner of business on the seventh day; but thou shalt keep holy the first day in its stead? This is a most important question, which I know not how you can answer. You are a Protestant, and you profess to go by the Bible and the Bible only; and yet in so important a matter as the observance of one day in seven as a holy day, you go against the plain letter of the Bible, and put another day in the place of that day which the Bible has commanded. The command to keep holy the seventh day is one of the ten commandments; you believe that the other nine are still binding; who gave you authority to tamper with the fourth? If you are consistent with your own principles, if you really follow the Bible and the Bible only, you ought to be able to produce some portion of the New Testament in which this fourth commandment is expressly altered."
   - **Significance**: Catholic apologetic directly challenging Protestant inconsistency in keeping Sunday while claiming "Bible only"

23. **Monsignor Louis Segur, Plain Talk about the Protestantism of Today**, p. 213:
   - Catholic critique of Protestant inconsistency
   - **Quote**: "The observance of Sunday by the Protestants is an homage they pay, in spite of themselves, to the authority of the [Catholic] Church."
   - **Significance**: Points out contradiction in rejecting Catholic authority while keeping Catholic Sunday

24. **Albert Smith, Chancellor of the Archdiocese of Baltimore**, letter dated February 10, 1920:
   - Official Church correspondence affirming Sunday change authority, replying for Cardinal
   - **Quote**: "If Protestants would follow the Bible, they should worship God on the Sabbath Day by God is Saturday. In keeping the Sunday, they are following a law of the Catholic Church."
   - **Significance**: Official Church representative stating Protestants follow Catholic law, not Bible, in Sunday observance

25. **The Faith of Millions** (Rev. John A. O'Brien, PhD):
   - Popular Catholic apologetic work
   - **Quote**: "Since Saturday, not Sunday, is specified in the Bible, isn't it curious that non-Catholics who profess to take their religion directly from the Bible and not from the Church, observe Sunday instead of Saturday? Yes, of course, it is inconsistent; but this change was made about fifteen centuries before Protestantism was born, and by that time the custom was universally observed. They have continued the custom, even though it rests upon the authority of the Catholic Church and not upon an explicit text in the Bible. That observance remains as a reminder of the Mother Church from which the non-Catholic sects broke away—like a boy running away from home but still carrying in his pocket a picture of his mother or a lock of her hair."
   - **Significance**: Widely distributed Catholic book pointing out Protestant inconsistency, describing Sunday as "reminder of the Mother Church"

26. **Catholic Record**, September 1, 1923:
   - Catholic periodical
   - **Quote**: "Sunday is our MARK of authority... The church is above the Bible, and this transference of Sabbath observance is proof of that fact."
   - **Significance**: Explicitly calls Sunday the "MARK of authority" proving Church is above Bible

27. **James Cardinal Gibbons, The Faith of Our Fathers**:
   - 88th edition, page 89 (Originally published 1876, republished 1980 by TAN Books)
   - One of the most influential Catholic apologetic books in American history
   - **Quote**: "You may read the Bible from Genesis to Revelation, and you will not find a single line authorizing the sanctification of Sunday. The Scriptures enforce the religious observance of Saturday, a day which we never sanctify."
   - **Additional Quote** (pages 72-73): "Reason and sense demand the acceptance of one or the other of these alternatives: either Protestantism and the keeping holy of Saturday, or Catholicity and the keeping holy of Sunday. Compromise is impossible."
   - **Significance**: Cardinal Gibbons, Archbishop of Baltimore, explicitly states choice is between biblical Saturday or Catholic Sunday—"compromise is impossible"

27a. **James Cardinal Gibbons, Archbishop of Baltimore, in a signed letter**:
   - Personal signed letter from Cardinal Gibbons (1877-1921)
   - **Quote**: "Is Saturday the seventh day according to the Bible and the Ten Commandments? I answer yes. Is Sunday the first day of the week and did the Church change the seventh day—Saturday—for Sunday, the first day? I answer yes. Did Christ change the day? I answer no!"
   - **Significance**: Cardinal Gibbons' personal signed statement explicitly admitting: (1) Saturday is the biblical seventh day, (2) Church changed it to Sunday, (3) Christ did NOT change it—direct admission from highest American Catholic authority

28. **The Catholic Virginian, "To Tell You The Truth,"** Vol. 22, No. 49 (October 3, 1947):
   - Diocesan newspaper
   - **Quote**: "I have repeatedly offered $1,000 to anyone who can furnish any proof from the Bible that Sunday is the day we are bound to keep... The Bible says, 'Remember the Sabbath day to keep it holy,' but the Catholic Church says, 'No, keep the first day of the week,' and the whole world bows down in obedience."
   - **Significance**: Mid-20th century reaffirmation of no biblical basis for Sunday

29. **Daniel Ferres, ed., Manual of Christian Doctrine** (1916):
   - Page 67
   - Catholic doctrinal manual with official Church approval
   - **Quote**: "Question: How prove you that the Church hath power to command feasts and holy days? Answer: By the very act of changing the Sabbath into Sunday, which Protestants allow of; and therefore they fondly contradict themselves, by keeping Sunday strictly, and breaking most other feasts commanded by the same Church."
   - **Significance**: Early 20th-century Catholic manual pointing out Protestant inconsistency—accepting Church authority for Sunday while rejecting it for other practices

30. **Martin J. Scott, Things Catholics Are Asked About** (1927):
   - Page 136
   - Popular Catholic Q&A book addressing Protestant inquiries
   - **Quote**: "Nowhere in the Bible do we find that Christ or the Apostles ordered that the Sabbath be changed from Saturday to Sunday. We have the commandment of God given to Moses to keep holy the Sabbath day, that is the 7th day of the week, Saturday. Today most Christians keep Sunday because it has been revealed to us by the [Catholic] church outside the Bible."
   - **Significance**: 1920s Catholic apologetics openly admitting change came from Church tradition "outside the Bible," not from Scripture

31. **Peter R. Kraemer, Catholic Church Extension Society**:
   - Catholic Church Extension Society official statement
   - **Quote**: "Regarding the change from the observance of the Jewish Sabbath to the Christian Sunday, I wish to draw your attention to the facts: (1) That Protestants, who accept the Bible as the only rule of faith and religion, should by all means go back to the observance of the Sabbath. The fact that they do not, but on the contrary observe the Sunday, stultifies them in the eyes of every thinking man. (2) We Catholics do not accept the Bible as the only rule of faith. Besides the Bible we have the living Church, the authority of the Church, as a rule to guide us. We say, this Church, instituted by Christ to teach and guide man through life, has the right to change the ceremonial laws of the Old Testament and hence, we accept her change of the Sabbath to Sunday. We frankly say, yes, the Church made this change, made this law, as she made many other laws, for instance, the Friday abstinence, the unmarried priesthood, the laws concerning mixed marriages, the regulation of Catholic marriages and a thousand other laws."
   - **Significance**: Catholic Church Extension Society comprehensive statement admitting Church authority alone changed Sabbath, challenging Protestants who accept the change while rejecting Catholic authority

32. **Controversial Catechism by Stephen Keenan**:
   - New Edition, revised by Rev. George Cormack, 1896
   - Pages 6, 7
   - **Q**: "Have you any other way of proving that the Church has power to institute festivals of precept?"
   - **A**: "Had she not such power... she could not have substituted the observance of Sunday the first day of the week, for the observance of Saturday the seventh day, a change for which there is no Scriptural authority."
   - **Significance**: Apologetic catechism designed to answer Protestant objections, using Sunday as proof of Church authority

33. **Rev. Stephen Keenan, A Doctrinal Catechism**, New York, 1857:
   - **Page 174** - **Q**: "Have you any other way of proving that the Church has power to institute festivals of precept?"
   - **A**: "Had she not such power, she could not have done that in which all modern religionists agree with her—she could not have substituted the observance of Sunday, the first day of the week, for the observance of Saturday, the seventh day, a change for which there is no Scriptural authority."
   - **Page 101** - **Quote**: "The Catholic Church of its own infallible authority created Sunday a holy day to take the place of the Sabbath of the old law."
   - **Significance**: Multiple references with Imprimatur (official Church approval) showing systematic teaching that Church changed Sabbath by its own authority

34. **This Rock, The Magazine of Catholic Apologetics and Evangelization**, June 1997, p. 8:
   - Modern Catholic apologetics magazine
   - **Quote**: "Fundamentalists... have denied that the Catholic Church has any authority to change Scripture. Yet they all accept the Catholic Church's decision to transfer the Sabbath to Sunday."
   - **Significance**: Late 20th-century affirmation showing continued consistency, challenging Protestant acceptance of Catholic change

35. **Our Sunday Visitor**, February 5, 1950:
   - Major Catholic weekly newspaper
   - **Quote**: "Practically everything Protestants regard as essential or important they have received from the Catholic Church... The Protestant mind does not seem to realize that in accepting the Bible and observing the Sunday, in keeping Christmas and Easter, they are accepting the authority of the spokesman for the Catholic Church."
   - **Significance**: States Protestants accept Catholic authority by keeping Sunday

36. **Priest Brady, address reported in Elizabeth, NJ 'News'**, March 18, 1903:
   - Public statement by Catholic priest in secular newspaper
   - **Quote**: "It is well to remind the Presbyterians, Baptists, Methodists, and all other Christians, that the Bible does not support them anywhere in their observance of Sunday. Sunday is an institution of the Roman Catholic Church, and those who observe the day observe a commandment of the Catholic Church."
   - **Significance**: Early 20th-century public statement challenging all Protestant denominations

37. **Dictionary of the Liturgy by Rev. Jovian P. Lang, O.F.M.**:
   - Comprehensive Catholic liturgical reference
   - **On Sunday Mass**: Explains that Sunday Mass attendance is the primary distinguishing mark of Catholic practice
   - **On the Eucharist**: Describes the "Blessed Sacrament" as central to Catholic identity and worship
   - **Key Teaching**: Sunday observance combined with Eucharistic celebration constitutes the fundamental mark of Catholic Church membership
   - **Significance**: Official liturgical dictionary identifying Sunday worship and Eucharist as defining marks of Catholic identity

38. **The Catechism of Perseverance: An Historical, Dogmatical, Moral, Liturgical, Apologetical, Philosophical and Social Exposition of Religion**:
   - Comprehensive Catholic catechetical work
   - **On Sunday Observance**: Presents Sunday as the "Lord's Day" instituted by Church authority
   - **On the Eucharist as Mark**: Teaches that reception of the Eucharist on Sunday is the distinguishing mark of Catholic faithful
   - **Key Doctrine**: "The Sunday Mass obligation and reception of the Blessed Sacrament are the marks by which Catholics are known and distinguished from all other religionists."
   - **Significance**: Comprehensive doctrinal work explicitly identifying Sunday Mass and Eucharist as the "marks" distinguishing Catholics

39. **Apostolic Letter Dies Domini of the Holy Father John Paul II to the Bishops, Clergy and Faithful of the Catholic Church on Keeping the Lord's Day** (1998):
   - Full title: *Dies Domini: On Keeping the Lord's Day Holy*
   - Papal apostolic letter addressed to entire Catholic hierarchy and laity
   - **On Sunday as Mark of Identity**: 
     - States that Sunday observance is "at the heart of [the Church's] life" and a "distinguishing mark" of Catholic identity
     - Describes Sunday as "the day which recalls... the beginning of the new creation"
   - **On the Eucharist**: 
     - Emphasizes Sunday Eucharist as "the heart of Sunday" observance
     - States: "The Sunday Eucharist is the fundamental response to the commandment to 'keep holy' the Lord's Day"
   - **Key Quote**: "Sunday is the day which is at the very heart of the Christian life... It is a sign of the Church's identity" (Section 81)
   - **Additional Quote on Mark**: "The Lord's Day has always been understood by the Church as a 'distinguishing sign' of her children" (Section 30)
   - **On Obligation**: Declares Sunday Mass attendance "not a matter of choice" but "duty" showing "loyalty to Christ and to his Church"
   - **Significance**: Modern papal document (1998) explicitly calling Sunday observance and Eucharist the "distinguishing mark" and "sign of identity" for Catholics—using prophetic language of Revelation 13-14 regarding the "mark"

**Catholic Apologetic Works Acknowledging the Change**:
- Multiple Catholic apologetic books and tracts from 19th-20th centuries spanning 1833-1997
- Consistent theme across over 160 years: Catholics don't deny changing Sabbath to Sunday; they claim authority to do so
- Challenge to Protestants: If you follow the Bible alone (sola scriptura), why keep Sunday?
- Sources include: official catechisms, cardinal statements, papal letters, theological studies, apologetic pamphlets, diocesan newspapers, educational textbooks, scholarly journals

**Significance of Catholic Admissions**:

The Catholic Church has been **remarkably consistent and honest** about the Sabbath change:

1. **They admit there is no biblical basis for Sunday observance**
2. **They claim church tradition and authority made the change**
3. **They openly challenge Protestants** who claim "Bible only" yet keep Sunday
4. **They present Sunday observance as proof of church authority** over Scripture

These Catholic sources are particularly valuable because they:
- Come from official Catholic publications
- Are not disputed by Catholic scholars
- Frankly acknowledge what happened
- Use the change as evidence of Catholic Church authority
- Present a logical challenge to Protestant inconsistency

The Catholic position is essentially: **"We changed it. We had the authority to change it. If you reject our authority, why do you keep our change?"**

This makes Sunday observance among Protestants particularly problematic, as they retain a purely Catholic tradition while rejecting Catholic authority—the very inconsistency Catholic apologists point out in these documents.

### Protestant Churches' Admissions on Sunday Observance (60 Denominational Statements)

**Official Protestant Statements Acknowledging No Biblical Authority for Sunday**:

While Catholics openly claim authority to change the Sabbath, Protestant churches face a more difficult position: most acknowledge Sunday has no biblical basis, yet continue observing it despite their doctrine of *sola scriptura* (Bible alone). The following **60 statements from Protestant theologians, pastors, and denominational publications** reveal this shocking inconsistency:

1. **Isaac Williams, *Plain Sermons on the Catechism*** (Vol. 1, pp. 334, 336):
   - Anglican clergyman and theologian
   - **Admission**: Acknowledged that Sunday observance has no direct biblical command
   - **Significance**: High Church Anglican tradition, which retained many Catholic practices, admitted the biblical Sabbath (Saturday) was changed without scriptural authority

2. **Canon Eyton, *The Ten Commandments*** (pp. 52, 63, 65):
   - Anglican canon (church official)
   - **Admission**: Acknowledged that the Fourth Commandment specifies the seventh day (Saturday), and that the change to Sunday (first day) came from church tradition, not Scripture
   - **Significance**: Church of England official admitting the commandment itself was not changed by biblical authority

3. **Bishop Seymour, *Why We Keep Sunday***:
   - Episcopal bishop
   - **Admission**: Wrote defending Sunday observance while acknowledging it was not commanded in Scripture
   - **Significance**: Even a work titled defending Sunday keeping had to admit it lacks biblical foundation

4. **Dr. Edward T. Hiscox, paper read before a New York ministers' conference** (Nov. 13, 1893, reported in *New York Examiner*, Nov. 16, 1893):
   - Baptist minister and author of *The Baptist Manual*
   - **Quote**: "There was and is a commandment to keep holy the Sabbath day, but that Sabbath day was not Sunday. It will be said, however, and with some show of triumph, that the Sabbath was transferred from the seventh to the first day of the week... Where can the record of such a transaction be found? Not in the New Testament absolutely not. There is no scriptural evidence of the change of the Sabbath institution from the seventh to the first day of the week."
   - **Additional Quote**: "To me it seems unaccountable that Jesus, during three years' discussion with His disciples, often conversing with them upon the Sabbath question... never alluded to any transference of the day; also, that during forty days of His resurrection life, no such thing was intimated. Of course, I quite well know that Sunday did come into use in early Christian history... But what a pity it comes branded with the mark of paganism, and christened with the name of the sun god, adopted and sanctioned by the papal apostasy, and bequeathed as a sacred legacy to Protestantism!"
   - **Significance**: Prominent Baptist minister, speaking to fellow ministers, admitted: (1) No scriptural evidence for the change, (2) Jesus never mentioned it, (3) Sunday comes "branded with the mark of paganism," (4) It was "adopted and sanctioned by the papal apostasy," (5) Protestantism received it as a "legacy" from Rome

5. **William Owen Carver, *The Lord's Day in Our Day*** (p. 49):
   - Southern Baptist theologian and professor
   - **Admission**: Acknowledged that neither Jesus nor the apostles instituted Sunday observance, and that it developed through church tradition
   - **Significance**: Baptist theological scholarship admitting Sunday observance is traditional, not biblical

6. **Dr. R. W. Dale, *The Ten Commandments*** (New York: Eaton & Mains, pp. 127-129):
   - Congregationalist minister and theologian
   - **Quote**: "It is quite clear that however rigidly or devotedly we may spend Sunday, we are not keeping the Sabbath... The Sabbath was founded on a specific Divine command. We can plead no such command for the obligation to observe Sunday... There is not a single sentence in the New Testament to suggest that we incur any penalty by violating the supposed sanctity of Sunday."
   - **Significance**: Congregationalist scholar explicitly stating: (1) Sunday is not the Sabbath, (2) No divine command for Sunday, (3) No New Testament penalty for not keeping Sunday

7. **Timothy Dwight, *Theology: Explained and Defended*** (1823, Sermon 107, Vol. 3, p. 258):
   - Congregationalist minister, President of Yale University
   - **Admission**: Acknowledged that the Sabbath commandment specifies the seventh day, and that Christian observance of the first day came from apostolic practice (tradition), not explicit biblical command
   - **Significance**: Leading American theologian and educator admitting Sunday observance rests on tradition rather than commandment

8. **Alexander Campbell, *The Christian Baptist*** (Feb. 2, 1824, Vol. 1, No. 7, p. 164):
   - Founder of the Disciples of Christ (Campbellite) movement
   - **Quote**: "But,' say some, 'it was changed from the seventh to the first day.' Where? when? and by whom? No, it never was changed, nor could it be, unless creation was to be gone through again: for the reason assigned must be changed before the observance, or respect to the reason, can be changed. It is all old wives' fables to talk of the change of the Sabbath from the seventh to the first day. If it be changed, it was that august personage changed it who changes times and laws *ex officio* – I think his name is *Doctor Antichrist*."
   - **Significance**: Restoration movement founder explicitly stating: (1) The Sabbath was never changed, (2) It could not be changed without re-doing creation, (3) Anyone claiming to change it is "Doctor Antichrist" (the power that "changes times and laws" from Daniel 7:25)

9. **First Day Observance** (pp. 17, 19):
   - Protestant pamphlet examining Sunday observance
   - **Admission**: Acknowledged that first-day observance developed in church history, not from biblical mandate
   - **Significance**: Even Protestant literature defending Sunday had to admit its non-biblical origin

10. **The Sunday Problem, a study book of the United Lutheran Church** (1923, p. 36):
    - Official Lutheran Church study publication
    - **Admission**: "We have seen how gradually the impression of the Jewish Sabbath faded from the mind of the Christian Church, and how completely the later Lord's Day took its place. But what a pity that it comes branded with the mark of Paganism, and christened with the name of the sun-god, then adopted and sanctioned by the Papal apostasy, and bequeathed as a sacred legacy to Protestantism."
    - **Significance**: Official Lutheran study book admitting: (1) Sunday "comes branded with the mark of Paganism," (2) Named after the sun-god, (3) "Adopted and sanctioned by the Papal apostasy," (4) "Bequeathed as a sacred legacy to Protestantism"—remarkable admission that Protestants inherited papal Sunday from Rome

11. **Augsburg Confession of Faith, Article 28** (written by Melanchthon, approved by Martin Luther, 1530; published in *The Book of Concord of the Evangelical Lutheran Church*, Henry Jacobs, ed., 1911, p. 63):
    - Foundational Lutheran confession of faith
    - **Quote**: "They [the Catholics] allege the Sabbath changed into Sunday, the Lord's day, contrary to the Decalogue, as it appears, neither is there any example more boasted of than the changing of the Sabbath day. Great, say they, is the power and authority of the church, since it dispensed with one of the Ten Commandments."
    - **Significance**: Luther's own confession admitting: (1) Catholics changed Sabbath to Sunday "contrary to the Decalogue" (Ten Commandments), (2) Catholics boast this change proves church authority, (3) This involves "dispensing with one of the Ten Commandments"—yet Lutherans continued observing Sunday

12. **Dr. Augustus Neander, *The History of the Christian Religion and Church*** (Henry John Rose, tr., 1843, p. 186):
    - German Lutheran church historian
    - **Quote**: "The festival of Sunday, like all other festivals, was always only a human ordinance, and it was far from the intentions of the apostles to establish a Divine command in this respect, far from them, and from the early apostolic Church, to transfer the laws of the Sabbath to Sunday."
    - **Significance**: Prominent Lutheran historian explicitly stating: (1) Sunday is "only a human ordinance," (2) Apostles never intended to establish it as divine command, (3) Early church did not transfer Sabbath laws to Sunday

13. **John Theodore Mueller, *Sabbath or Sunday*** (pp. 15, 16):
    - Lutheran theologian
    - **Admission**: Acknowledged that the Sabbath commandment specifies Saturday (seventh day), and that Sunday observance came from church tradition
    - **Significance**: Lutheran scholarship admitting Sunday is tradition, not biblical commandment

14. **Harris Franklin Rall, *Christian Advocate*** (July 2, 1942, p. 26):
    - Methodist theologian and professor
    - **Quote**: "Take the matter of Sunday. There are indications in the New Testament as to how the church came to keep the first day of the week as its day of worship, but there is no passage telling Christians to keep that day, or to transfer the Jewish Sabbath to that day."
    - **Significance**: Methodist scholar admitting: (1) No passage tells Christians to keep Sunday, (2) No passage authorizes transferring the Sabbath

15. **John Wesley, *The Works of the Rev. John Wesley, A.M.*** (John Emory, ed., New York: Eaton & Mains, Sermon 25, Vol. 1, p. 221):
    - Founder of Methodism
    - **Quote**: "But, the moral law contained in the ten commandments, and enforced by the prophets, he [Christ] did not take away. It was not the design of his coming to revoke any part of this. This is a law which never can be broken... Every part of this law must remain in force upon all mankind, and in all ages; as not depending either on time or place, or any other circumstances liable to change, but on the nature of God and the nature of man, and their unchangeable relation to each other."
    - **Significance**: Wesley taught that the Ten Commandments (including the fourth commandment Sabbath) are unchangeable moral law binding on all humanity—yet the Methodist church he founded observes Sunday, not the seventh-day Sabbath commanded in the Fourth Commandment

16. **D. L. Moody, *Weighed and Wanting*** (Fleming H. Revell Co.: New York, pp. 47, 48):
    - Famous evangelist, founder of Moody Bible Institute
    - **Quote**: "The Sabbath was binding in Eden, and it has been in force ever since. This fourth commandment begins with the word 'remember,' showing that the Sabbath already existed when God wrote the law on the tables of stone at Sinai. How can men claim that this one commandment has been done away with when they will admit that the other nine are still binding?"
    - **Significance**: Moody taught that the Sabbath commandment is still binding and has been in force since Eden—yet observed Sunday rather than the seventh-day Sabbath specified in the commandment

17. **T. C. Blake, D.D., *Theology Condensed*** (pp. 474, 475):
    - Presbyterian theologian
    - **Admission**: Acknowledged that the seventh day is the Sabbath according to the commandment, and that the change to Sunday observance came through church history and tradition
    - **Significance**: Presbyterian scholarship admitting Sunday is based on tradition, not the biblical commandment

---

#### **ADDITIONAL DENOMINATIONAL ADMISSIONS - Expanded Collection**

**Southern Baptist Additional Quotes**:

18. **Joseph Hudson Taylor, *The Sabbatic Question*** (pp. 14-17, 41):
    - Southern Baptist theologian
    - **Quote**: "The sacred name of the Seventh day is Sabbath. This fact is too clear to require argument [Exodus 20:10 quoted]… on this point the plain teaching of the Word has been admitted in all ages… Not once did the disciples apply the Sabbath law to the first day of the week, -- that folly was left for a later age, nor did they pretend that the first day supplanted the seventh."
    - **Significance**: Baptist scholar calling it "folly" to apply Sabbath law to Sunday, admitting disciples never made this change

19. **Adult Quarterly, Southern Baptist Convention series** (Aug. 15, 1937):
    - Official Southern Baptist publication
    - **Quote**: "The first four commandments set forth man's obligations directly toward God.... But when we keep the first four commandments, we are likely to keep the other six.... The fourth commandment sets forth God's claim on man's time and thought.... The six days of labour and the rest on the Sabbath are to be maintained as a witness to God's toil and rest in the creation.... No one of the ten words is of merely racial significance.... The Sabbath was established originally (long before Moses) in no special connection with the Hebrews, but as an institution for all mankind, in commemoration of God's rest after the six days of creation. It was designed for all the descendants of Adam."
    - **Significance**: Official Southern Baptist teaching that: (1) The Sabbath is for all mankind, not just Jews, (2) Established at Creation before Moses, (3) Part of the Ten Commandments binding on all humanity

**Presbyterian Additional Quotes**:

20. **Dwight's Theology** (Vol. 14, p. 401):
    - Presbyterian systematic theology
    - **Quote**: "The Christian Sabbath (Sunday) is not in the Scriptures, and was not by the primitive church called the Sabbath."
    - **Significance**: Presbyterian theology admitting Sunday was never called "Sabbath" in Scripture or early church

21. **Jonathan Edwards, *Works*** (Vol. 4, p. 621):
    - Presbyterian/Congregationalist theologian
    - **Quote**: "A further argument for the perpetuity of the Sabbath we have in Matthew 24:20, Pray ye that your flight be not in the winter neither on the Sabbath day. But the final destruction of Jerusalem was after the Christian dispensation was fully set up (AD 70). Yet it is plainly implied in these words of the Lord that even then Christians were bound to strict observation of the Sabbath."
    - **Significance**: Edwards noting that Jesus expected Sabbath observance 40 years after the cross (AD 70), proving it wasn't abolished

22. **John Calvin, *Commentary on a Harmony of the Gospels*** (Vol. 1, page 277):
    - Presbyterian/Reformed founder
    - **Quote**: "We must not imagine that the coming of Christ has freed us from the authority of the law; for it is the eternal rule of a devout and holy life, and must therefore be as unchangeable as the justice of God, which it embraced, is constant and uniform."
    - **Significance**: Calvin taught the moral law (Ten Commandments) is "eternal" and "unchangeable"—yet Reformed churches observe Sunday, not the seventh-day Sabbath commanded in the Fourth Commandment

23. **American Presbyterian Board of Publication, Tract No. 175**:
    - Official Presbyterian publication
    - **Quote**: "God instituted the Sabbath at the creation of man, setting apart the seventh day for the purpose, and imposed its observance as a universal and perpetual moral obligation upon the race."
    - **Significance**: Presbyterian official teaching that Sabbath is "universal and perpetual" moral obligation

24. **American Presbyterian Board of Publication, Tract No. 118**:
    - Official Presbyterian publication
    - **Quote**: "The observance of the seventh-day Sabbath did not cease till it was abolished after the [Roman] empire became Christian..."
    - **Significance**: Presbyterian admission that seventh-day Sabbath was only "abolished" when the Roman Empire became Christian (under Constantine)—not by biblical authority

25. **Westminster Confession of Faith, Chap. 19, Art. 5**:
    - Foundational Presbyterian confession (still official doctrine)
    - **Quote**: "The moral law doth for ever bind all, as well justified persons as others, to the obedience thereof; and that not only in regard to the matter contained in it, but also in respect of the authority of God the Creator who gave it. Neither doth Christ in the gospel in any way dissolve, but much strengthen this obligation."
    - **Significance**: Presbyterian confession stating moral law (Ten Commandments) binds all forever, Christ did not dissolve it—yet Presbyterians observe Sunday instead of the seventh-day Sabbath commanded in the Fourth Commandment

**Methodist Additional Quotes**:

26. **Methodist Church Discipline** (1904, page 23):
    - Official Methodist doctrinal statement
    - **Quote**: "No Christian whatsoever is free from the obedience of the commandments which are called moral."
    - **Significance**: Official Methodist teaching that all Christians must obey the moral commandments (Ten Commandments)—yet Methodist church observes Sunday, not Saturday Sabbath

27. **E.O. Haven, *Pillars of Truth*** (page 88):
    - Methodist theologian
    - **Quote**: "The Sabbath was made for MAN; not for the Hebrews, but for all men."
    - **Significance**: Methodist scholar affirming Sabbath is universal, not just for Jews

28. **Clovis G. Chappell, *Ten Rules for Living*** (page 61):
    - Methodist minister
    - **Quote**: "The reason we observe the first day instead of the seventh is based on no positive command. One will search the Scriptures in vain for authority for changing from the seventh day to the first. The early Christians began to worship on the first day of the week because Jesus rose from the dead on that day. By and by, this day of worship was made also a day of rest, a legal holiday. This took place in the year 321.... The reason we observe the first day instead of the seventh is based on no positive command. One will search the Scriptures in vain for authority for changing from the seventh day to the first... Our Christian Sabbath, therefore, is not a matter of positive command. It is a gift of the church..."
    - **Significance**: Methodist admission: (1) No scriptural authority for the change, (2) Sunday became a legal holiday in 321 (Constantine's decree), (3) Sunday is "a gift of the church" not biblical command

29. **Charles Buck, *A Theological Dictionary*** (under "Sabbath"):
    - Methodist theologian
    - **Quote**: "Sabbath in the Hebrew language signifies rest, and is the seventh day of the week... and it must be confessed that there is no law in the New Testament concerning the first day."
    - **Significance**: Methodist theological reference work admitting no New Testament law for Sunday

30. **Sunday School Advocate** (Dec. 31, 1921):
    - Methodist publication
    - **Quote**: "In the days of very long ago the people of the world began to give names to everything... The people became Christians and were ruled by an emperor whose name was Constantine. This emperor made Sunday the Christian Sabbath, because of the blessing of light and heat which came from the sun. So our Sunday is a sun-day, isn't it?"
    - **Significance**: Methodist Sunday School material admitting Sunday comes from sun-worship and Constantine's decree, not biblical command

**Lutheran Additional Quotes (Free Church)**:

31. **George Sverdrup, *A New Day*** (Lutheran Free Church):
    - Lutheran theologian
    - **Quote**: "For when there could not be produced one solitary place in the Holy Scriptures which testified that either the Lord Himself or the apostles had ordered such a transfer of the Sabbath to Sunday, then it was not easy to answer the question: Who has transferred the Sabbath, and who has the right to do it?"
    - **Significance**: Lutheran Free Church leader acknowledging: (1) No Scripture shows Jesus or apostles changed Sabbath to Sunday, (2) Question remains unanswered: Who has the right to change God's commandment?

**Lutheran Additional Quotes**:

32. **Martin Luther, *Spiritual Antichrist*** (pages 71, 72):
    - Lutheran Reformation founder
    - **Quote**: "I wonder exceedingly how it came to be imputed to me that I should reject the law of Ten Commandments...Whosoever abrogates the law must of necessity abrogate sin also."
    - **Significance**: Luther himself taught the Ten Commandments (including the Sabbath) cannot be abrogated—yet Lutheran church observes Sunday

**Episcopal/Anglican Additional Quotes**:

33. **Phillip Carrington, Archbishop of Quebec**, quoted in *Toronto Daily Star* (Oct 26, 1949):
    - Anglican archbishop
    - **Quote**: "The Bible commandment says on the seventh-day thou shalt rest. That is Saturday. Nowhere in the Bible is it laid down that worship should be done on Sunday."
    - **Significance**: Anglican archbishop publicly stating in major newspaper: (1) Bible commands seventh-day (Saturday) rest, (2) Bible never commands Sunday worship
    - **Additional Context**: Carrington spoke this in a message delivered to a packed assembly of clergymen, widely reported in news media at the time

34. **Rev. Lionel Beere, All-Saints Church, Ponsonby, N.Z.**, in *Church and People* (Sept. 1, 1947):
    - Anglican rector
    - **Quote**: "Many people think that Sunday is the Sabbath. But neither in the New Testament nor in the early church is there anything to suggest that we have any right to transfer the observance of the seventh day of the week to the first. The Sabbath was and is Saturday and not Sunday, and if it were binding on us then we should observe it on that day, and on no other."
    - **Significance**: Anglican minister clearly stating: (1) Sunday is not the Sabbath, (2) No right to transfer seventh day to first day, (3) If Sabbath is binding, it must be Saturday

35. **Rev. Isaac Williams, *Ser. on Catechism*** (p. 334):
    - Anglican clergyman
    - **Quote**: "Where are we told in Scripture that we are to keep the first day at all? We are commanded to keep the Seventh; but we are nowhere commanded to keep the first day. The reason why we keep the first day holy instead of the seventh is for the same reason that we observe many things, not because the Bible, but because the Church, has enjoined them."
    - **Significance**: Anglican admission: (1) No Scripture commands keeping first day, (2) We keep Sunday because the Church commanded it, not the Bible

36. **Rev. Geo. Hodges**:
    - Anglican minister
    - **Quote**: "The seventh day, the commandment says, is the Sabbath of The Lord thy God. No kind of arithmetic, no kind of almanac, can make seven equal one, nor the seventh mean the first, nor Saturday mean Sunday.... The fact is that we are all Sabbath breakers, every one of us."
    - **Significance**: Anglican minister admitting: (1) The commandment clearly says seventh day, (2) No mathematical trick makes seventh = first, (3) Sunday-keepers are "Sabbath breakers"

37. **Sir William Domville, *Examination of the Six Texts*** (pages 6, 7, Supplement):
    - Anglican scholar
    - **Quote**: "Not any ecclesiastical writer of the first three centuries attributed the origin of Sunday observance either to Christ or to His apostles."
    - **Significance**: Historical research showing early church writers (first 300 years) never claimed Christ or apostles instituted Sunday

38. **Bishop Jeremy Taylor, *Ductor Dubitantium*** (Part I, Book II, Chap. 2, Rule 6, Sec. 51, 59):
    - Anglican bishop
    - **Quote**: "The Lord's day did not succeed in the place of the Sabbath....The Lord's day was merely an ecclesiastical institution. It was not introduced by virtue of the fourth commandment, because for almost three hundred years together they kept that day which was in that commandment...The primitive Christians did all manner of works upon the Lord's day, even in times of persecution, when they are the strictest observers of all the divine commandments; but in this they knew there was none."
    - **Significance**: Anglican bishop admitting: (1) Sunday did not replace Sabbath, (2) Sunday is "merely an ecclesiastical institution," (3) For 300 years Christians kept the seventh day commanded in the Fourth Commandment, (4) Early Christians worked on Sunday because they knew there was no divine command against it

39. **T.M. Morer, *Dialogues on the Lord's Day*** (pages 22, 23):
    - Anglican theologian
    - **Quote**: "Sunday being the day on which the Gentiles solemnly adore that planet and called it Sunday, partly from its influence on that day especially, and partly in respect to its divine body (as they conceived it), the Christians thought fit to keep the same day and the same name of it, that they might not appear causelessly peevish, and by that means hinder the conversion of the Gentiles, and bring a greater prejudice than might be otherwise taken against the gospel."
    - **Significance**: Anglican scholar admitting: (1) Sunday was pagan sun-worship day, (2) Christians adopted it to avoid appearing "peevish" to pagans, (3) Changed for evangelistic/pragmatic reasons, not biblical command

40. **D. Morse-Boycott, *Daily Herald, London*** (Feb. 26, 1931):
    - Anglican clergyman
    - **Quote**: "The Puritan idea was historically unhappy. It made Sunday into the Sabbath day. Even educated people call Sunday the Sabbath. Even clergymen do. But, unless my reckoning is all wrong, the Sabbath day lasts twenty-four hours from six o'clock on Friday evening. It gives over, therefore, before we come to Sunday. If you suggest to a Sabbatarian that he ought to observe the Sabbath on the proper day, you arouse no enthusiasm. He at once replies that the day, not the principle, has been changed. But changed by whom? There is no injunction in the whole of the New Testament to Christians to change the Sabbath into Sunday."
    - **Significance**: Anglican minister in major London newspaper admitting: (1) Sabbath is Friday evening to Saturday evening, (2) Sunday is not the Sabbath, (3) No New Testament command to change Sabbath to Sunday

41. **F.W. Farrar, D.D., *The Voice From Sinai*** (page 167):
    - Anglican Dean of Canterbury
    - **Quote**: "The Christian church made no formal, but a gradual and almost unconscious transference of the one day to the other."
    - **Significance**: Anglican leader admitting the change was "gradual and almost unconscious," not by divine decree

42. **Peter Heylyn, *History of the Sabbath*** (page 410):
    - Anglican historian
    - **Quote**: "Take which you will, either of the Fathers or the moderns, and we shall find no Lord's day instituted by any apostolical mandate; no Sabbath set on foot by them upon the first day of the week."
    - **Significance**: Historical research showing no apostolic command for Sunday observance

43. **Dr. Stephen, Bishop of Newcastle, N.S.W.**, address reported in *Newcastle Morning Herald* (May 14, 1924):
    - Anglican bishop
    - **Quote**: "Merely to denounce the tendency to secularise Sunday is as futile as it is easy. What we want is to find some principle, to which as Christians we can appeal, and on which we can base both our conduct and our advice. We turn to the New Testament, and we look in vain for any authoritative rule. There is no recorded word of Christ, there is no word of any of the apostles, which tells how we should keep Sunday, or indeed that we should keep it at all. It is disappointing, for it would make our task much easier if we could point to a definite rule, which left us no option but simple obedience or disobedience.... There is no rule for Sunday observance, either in Scripture or history."
    - **Significance**: Anglican bishop publicly admitting: (1) No word from Christ about Sunday, (2) No word from apostles about Sunday, (3) No rule for Sunday observance in Scripture or history

**Church of Christ/Disciples of Christ Additional Quotes**:

44. **Dr. D.H. Lucas, *Christian Oracle*** (January, 1890):
    - Church of Christ minister
    - **Quote**: "There is no direct Scriptural authority for designating the first day 'the Lord's Day.'"
    - **Significance**: Disciples of Christ scholar admitting no biblical basis for calling Sunday "the Lord's Day"

45. **G. Alridge, Editor, *The Bible Standard*** (April, 1916):
    - Church of Christ publication
    - **Quote**: "...If the fourth command is binding upon us Gentiles by all means keep it. But let those who demand a strict observance of the Sabbath remember that the seventh day is the ONLY sabbath day commanded, and God never repealed that command. If you would keep the Sabbath, keep it; but Sunday is not the Sabbath. The argument of the 'Seventh-day Adventists' is on one point unassailable. It is the Seventh day not the first day that the command refers to."
    - **Significance**: Church of Christ editor admitting: (1) Seventh day is the ONLY Sabbath commanded, (2) God never repealed that command, (3) Sunday is not the Sabbath, (4) Seventh-day Adventist argument is "unassailable" on this point

46. **Bible Standard** (Auckland, New Zealand, May, 1916):
    - Church of Christ publication
    - **Quote**: "But we do not find any direct command from God, or instruction from the risen Christ, or admonition from the early apostles, that the first day is to be substituted for the seventh day Sabbath.... Let us be clear on this point. Though to the Christian 'that day, the first day of the week' is the most memorable of all days... there is no command or warrant in the New Testament for observing it as a holy day. The Roman Church selected the first day of the week in honour of the resurrection of Christ...."
    - **Significance**: Official Church of Christ publication admitting: (1) No command from God for first day, (2) No instruction from Christ for first day, (3) No apostolic command for first day, (4) Roman Church selected Sunday

47. **Dr. N. Summerbell, *History of the Christian Church*** (Third Edition, page 415):
    - Christian Church historian
    - **Quote**: "It has reversed the fourth commandment by doing away with the Sabbath of God's Word, and instituting Sunday as a holiday."
    - **Significance**: Church historian stating the Fourth Commandment was "reversed" by church authority, not biblical warrant

**Congregational Additional Quotes**:

48. **Orin Fowler, A.M., *Mode and Subjects of Baptism***:
    - Congregationalist minister
    - **Quote**: "There is no command in the Bible requiring us to observe the first day of the week as the Christian Sabbath."
    - **Significance**: Congregationalist admission of no biblical command for Sunday

49. **Dr. Lyman Abbott, *Christian Union*** (Jan. 18, 1882):
    - Congregationalist minister and editor
    - **Quote**: "The current notion that Christ and His apostles authoritatively substituted the first day for the seventh, is absolutely without any authority in the New Testament."
    - **Significance**: Prominent Congregationalist leader stating change has "absolutely no authority in New Testament"

50. **Buck's Theological Dictionary** (page 403):
    - Congregationalist reference work
    - **Quote**: "It must be confessed that there is no law in the New Testament concerning the first day."
    - **Significance**: Theological dictionary admitting no New Testament law for first day

**Moody Bible Institute Additional Quote**:

51. **D.L. Moody** (at San Francisco, Jan. 1st, 1881):
    - Founder of Moody Bible Institute
    - **Quote**: "This Fourth is not a commandment for one place, or one time, but for all places and times."
    - **Significance**: Moody teaching the Fourth Commandment (Sabbath) is universal and perpetual

**Brethren Quotes**:

52. ***Words of Truth and Grace*** (p. 281):
    - Brethren publication
    - **Quote**: "With the views of the law and the Sabbath we once held... and which are still held by perhaps the great majority of the most earnest Christians, we confess that we could not answer Adventists. What is more, neither before or since have I heard or read what would conclusively answer an Adventist in his Scriptural contention that the Seventh day is the Sabbath (Ex. 20:10). It is not 'one day in seven' as some put it, but 'the seventh day according to the commandment.'"
    - **Significance**: Brethren admission: (1) Cannot answer Seventh-day Adventist argument, (2) Sabbath is not "one day in seven" but specifically "the seventh day," (3) No one has ever conclusively answered the Adventist biblical position

**Baptist Additional Quotes**:

53. **Harold Lindsell (editor), *Christianity Today*** (Nov. 5, 1976):
    - Baptist editor of major evangelical magazine
    - **Quote**: "There is nothing in Scripture that requires us to keep Sunday rather than Saturday as a holy day."
    - **Significance**: Major evangelical publication admitting no scriptural requirement for Sunday

54. ***The Watchman***:
    - Baptist publication
    - **Quote**: "The Scriptures nowhere call the first day of the week the Sabbath....There is no Scriptural authority for so doing, nor of course, any Scriptural obligation."
    - **Significance**: Baptist periodical admitting: (1) Scripture never calls Sunday "Sabbath," (2) No scriptural authority or obligation for Sunday

55. **William Owen Carver, *The Lord's Day in Our Day*** (page 49):
    - Southern Baptist theologian
    - **Quote**: "There was never any formal or authoritative change from the Jewish seventh-day Sabbath to the Christian first-day observance."
    - **Significance**: Baptist scholar admitting no formal or authoritative change occurred

**Miscellaneous Protestant Quotes**:

56. **The Library of Christian Doctrine** (pages 3, 4):
    - Protestant theological library series
    - **Quote**: "You will tell me that Saturday was the Jewish Sabbath, but that the Christian Sabbath has been changed to Sunday. Changed! But by whom? Who has authority to change an express commandment of Almighty God? When God has spoken and said, 'Thou shalt keep holy the seventh day,' who shall dare to say, 'Nay, thou mayest work and do all manner of business on the seventh day; but thou shalt keep holy the first day in its stead'? This is a most important question, which I know not how you can answer. You are a Protestant, and you profess to go by the Bible and the Bible only; and yet in so important a matter as the observance of one day in seven as a holy day, you go against the plain letter of the Bible, and put another day in the place of that day which the Bible has commanded. The command to keep holy the seventh day is one of the Ten Commandments; you believe that the other nine are still binding; who gave you authority to tamper with the fourth? If you are consistent with your own principles, if you really follow the Bible and the Bible only, you ought to be able to produce some portion of the New Testament in which this fourth commandment is expressly altered."
    - **Significance**: Protestant theological work challenging Protestants: (1) Who changed the commandment? (2) Protestants profess "Bible only" yet violate it, (3) If nine commandments are binding, why not the fourth? (4) Must produce biblical evidence for the change

57. **Fulton Oursler, *Cosmopolitan*** (Sept. 1951, pages 34, 35):
    - Protestant journalist and author
    - **Quote**: "Sabbath means, of course, Saturday, the seventh day of the week, but the early Christians changed the observance to Sunday, to honour the day on which Christ arose from the dead."
    - **Additional Quote**: "I do not pretend to be even an amateur scholar of the Scriptures. I read the Decalogue merely as an average man searching for guidance, and in the immortal 'Ten Words' I find a blueprint for the good life....Most certainly the Commandments are needed today, perhaps more than ever before. Their divine message confronts us with a profound moral challenge in an epidemic of evil; a unifying message acceptable alike to Jew, Moslem, and Christian. Who, reading the Ten in the light of history and of current events, can doubt their identity with the eternal law of nature?"
    - **Significance**: Popular Protestant writer admitting: (1) Sabbath means Saturday, (2) Early Christians (not apostles or Christ) changed it, (3) The Ten Commandments are eternal law needed today

58. **H. J. Flowers, B.A., B.D., *The Permanent Value of the Ten Commandments*** (page 13):
    - Protestant theologian
    - **Quote**: "The Sabbath is commanded to be kept on the seventh day. It could not be kept on any other day. To observe the first day of the week or the fourth is not to observe the Sabbath.... It was the last day of the week, after six days of work, that was to be kept holy. The observance of no other day would fulfil the law."
    - **Significance**: Protestant admission that: (1) Sabbath can ONLY be kept on seventh day, (2) First day observance is NOT Sabbath observance, (3) Only seventh day fulfills the law

59. **F. M. Setzler, Head Curator, Department of Anthropology, Smithsonian Institute** (letter dated Sept. 1, 1949):
    - Protestant scholar
    - **Quote**: "The evaluation of Sunday, the traditionally accepted day of the resurrection of Christ, has varied greatly throughout the centuries of the Christian Era. From time to time it has been confused with the seventh day of the week, the Sabbath. English-speaking peoples have been the most consistent in perpetuating the erroneous assumption that the obligation of the fourth commandment has passed over to Sunday. In popular speech, Sunday is frequently, but erroneously, spoken of as the Sabbath."
    - **Significance**: Smithsonian scholar (Protestant) admitting: (1) Sunday confused with Sabbath, (2) English-speaking peoples especially perpetuate this error, (3) Calling Sunday "Sabbath" is erroneous

60. **James G. Murphy, *Commentary on the Book of Exodus*** (comments on Exodus 20:8-11):
    - Protestant biblical commentator
    - **Quote**: "He that observes the Sabbath aright holds the history of that which it celebrates to be authentic, and therefore believes in the creation of the first man; in the creation of a fair abode for man in the space of six days; in the primeval and absolute creation of the heavens and the earth, and, as a necessary antecedent to all this, in the Creator, who at the close of His latest creative effort, rested on the seventh day. The Sabbath thus becomes a sign by which the believers in a historical revelation are distinguished from those who have allowed these great facts to fade from their remembrance."
    - **Significance**: Protestant commentary stating Sabbath observance is a sign distinguishing believers in biblical Creation from those who reject it

**Significance of Protestant Admissions**:

These Protestant statements reveal a profound inconsistency:

1. **Protestant Doctrine**: *Sola Scriptura* (Bible alone as authority) - The foundational principle of the Protestant Reformation
2. **Protestant Practice**: Sunday observance - Admittedly having no biblical basis

**The Protestant Dilemma**:
- **They reject papal authority** - The Reformation was about returning to biblical authority
- **They keep a papal tradition** - Sunday observance, which they admit has no biblical warrant
- **They admit the inconsistency** - Many Protestant theologians openly acknowledge Sunday has no scriptural basis
- **They continue the practice anyway** - Despite admitting it contradicts *sola scriptura*

**Key Protestant Admissions**:
- No biblical command for Sunday observance
- Jesus never mentioned changing the Sabbath
- The apostles never authorized the change
- Sunday observance developed through church tradition
- The change came from papal/Catholic authority
- Sunday "comes branded with the mark of paganism"
- Protestants inherited Sunday from Rome as "a sacred legacy"

**The Catholic Challenge Stands Unanswered**:

Catholic apologists have consistently challenged Protestants: **"If you claim 'Bible only,' why do you keep our Sunday?"**

These Protestant admissions show they have **no answer** to this challenge. They acknowledge:
- Sunday is not commanded in Scripture
- The Sabbath commandment specifies Saturday (seventh day)
- The change came from Catholic Church authority
- By keeping Sunday, they honor a Catholic tradition over biblical commandment

**Prophetic Significance**:

This Protestant admission is crucial for understanding Revelation 17's "daughters" of Babylon:
- **Mother**: Catholic Church (openly claims authority to change God's law)
- **Daughters**: Protestant churches (reject Catholic authority but retain Catholic Sunday)
- **"Drunk with her wine"**: Keep the false doctrine (Sunday) while claiming to follow Scripture alone

The Protestant churches' own theologians and leaders admit that by keeping Sunday, they:
1. **Contradict their own doctrine** of *sola scriptura*
2. **Honor Catholic tradition** over biblical commandment
3. **Accept papal authority** in practice while rejecting it in theory
4. **Perpetuate the change** that Daniel 7:25 predicted (the little horn "thinks to change times and law")

When Sunday laws are enforced globally, Protestant churches will have no theological ground to stand on—their own scholars have admitted for over 150 years that Sunday observance has no biblical basis. The Catholic Church can rightly say: **"You've been keeping our day all along. Now it becomes law."**

This is why Revelation 17:5 calls the Protestant churches "daughters" of Babylon—they came out of the mother church during the Reformation, but they **brought the wine (false doctrine) with them**. The most prominent example is Sunday observance, which these Protestant sources frankly admit is tradition, not Scripture.

### Methodology Note

This document synthesizes information from:
- Primary biblical sources (Old Testament, New Testament, Prophetic Books)
- Primary historical sources (ancient texts, church councils, imperial edicts, classical writers)
- Secondary academic scholarship (peer-reviewed journals, university press books)
- Theological commentaries (biblical prophecy interpretation, doctrinal studies)
- Legal documents (constitutions, statutes, court cases)
- Contemporary policy documents (2024-2025 initiatives)
- Religious organizational publications
- Catholic Church official statements and documents
- News sources and official websites (verified 2024-2025)

**Specific Prophetic Content**:
The prophetic sections (Daniel 2, Daniel 7, Revelation 13, Revelation 17, Revelation 20) draw from:
- Direct biblical text and context
- Historical fulfillment documentation (dates of empires, kingdoms, papal events)
- Classical historical sources (Roman Empire, barbarian kingdoms, Byzantine Empire)
- Scholarly prophetic commentaries (Maxwell, Smith, LaRondelle)
- Archaeological and historical verification of prophetic fulfillment

**Seven Hills of Rome**:
The identification of Rome as the city on seven hills is documented in:
- Classical Roman literature (Virgil, Plutarch, Cicero, Livy, Propertius)
- Historical geography of Rome (Septem Montes - established designation)
- Modern archaeological and geographical documentation
- Vatican City location within historic Rome

**Wine of Babylon Symbolism**:
The interpretation of "wine" as false doctrine draws from:
- Biblical usage in prophetic contexts (Jeremiah 51:7, Revelation 17-18)
- Historical documentation of doctrinal changes (Constantine era through medieval period)
- Catholic Church's own acknowledgment of changing biblical practices
- Comparative theology (biblical teaching vs. traditional teaching)

**Millennium Teaching**:
The biblical millennium interpretation is based on:
- Plain reading of Revelation 20:1-15 (six literal references to "thousand years")
- Cross-reference with supporting passages (1 Thessalonians 4:16-17, John 14:2-3, Jeremiah 4:23-26)
- Historical development tracking (early church premillennialism, Augustine's amillennialism ~400 CE)
- Harmony with other biblical doctrines (state of dead, resurrections, final judgment)
- Consistency in prophetic interpretation methodology

**Rapture Teaching**:
The analysis of "rapture" (being caught up) is based on:
- Direct biblical texts (1 Thessalonians 4:16-17, Matthew 24:27-31, Revelation 1:7)
- Historical documentation of secret rapture theory's origin (John Nelson Darby, 1830s)
- Comparison with early church teaching (no secret rapture doctrine found)
- Contextual analysis of key passages (Matthew 24:40-41, Luke 17:37)
- Theological consistency with related doctrines (immortal soul required for secret rapture)

All biblical quotations use standard biblical reference notation. Historical dates follow scholarly consensus. Contemporary information was verified through multiple sources and official organizational websites as of December 2025.

## Appendix: The Strategic Reading Order Explained

### This Study Requires Maximum Spiritual Discernment

> **1 Corinthians 2:14** - "The natural man does not receive the things of the Spirit of God, for they are foolishness to him; nor can he understand them, because they are spiritually discerned."

**This guide examines:**
- Complex prophecy (Daniel and Revelation)
- Challenging historical evidence (papal authority, Sabbath change)
- Emotionally difficult truths (your church tradition may be wrong)
- Life-altering decisions (leaving inherited beliefs, finding biblical truth)

**You cannot discern these truths if:**
- Your brain is suppressed by poor diet (sugar crashes, caffeine addiction, inflammation)
- Your mind is hijacked by media (dopamine addiction, frontal lobe suppression)
- Your spiritual sensitivity is dulled by physical/mental compromise

### The Strategic Progression Detailed

**1. START WITH: Daniel Diet Guide** (Weeks 1-4)
- **Why first:** Restores neurological function, removes stimulants that suppress frontal lobe
- **What happens:** Mental clarity, emotional stability, restored gut-brain connection
- **Result:** Your brain can now think clearly and critically

**2. NEXT: Media Influence Guide** (Weeks 5-8, while maintaining diet)
- **Why second:** Protects the mind you just restored, breaks dopamine addiction
- **What happens:** Restored attention span, moral sensitivity, spiritual awareness
- **Result:** Your mind can now focus on deep Bible study without distraction

**3. THIS GUIDE: Babylon's Wine** (Week 9+, while maintaining both)
- **Why last:** Requires sustained attention, logical reasoning, emotional stability, and willingness to act
- **What happens:** Conviction about biblical truth, understanding of prophecy, courage to obey God's commands
- **Result:** The Holy Spirit can guide you into all truth (John 16:13)

#### **Biblical Precedent: Daniel's Preparation**

**Daniel 1 (Diet) → Daniel 3 (Standing Firm) → Daniel 10 (Spiritual Vision)**

1. **Daniel 1:8-16** - Refused royal food, ate vegetables/water
   - Result: "Better in appearance and fatter in flesh" (physical health)

2. **Daniel 3:16-18** - Refused to worship golden image
   - Result: Delivered from fiery furnace (moral courage enabled by clear mind)

3. **Daniel 10:2-3** - 21-day fast, no meat/wine
   - Result: Angelic visitation, prophetic revelation (spiritual discernment)

**The progression is deliberate:** Physical preparation → Mental protection → Spiritual insight

### Why Many Reject Truth Despite Clear Evidence

Many will read this study and see the biblical evidence clearly, yet do nothing. Why?

**Not because the evidence is insufficient, but because:**
- **Brain fog** (from poor diet) prevents following complex arguments
- **Dopamine addiction** (from media) makes deep study feel boring
- **Emotional reactivity** (from compromised health) triggers defensiveness
- **Weakened willpower** (from stimulants) makes change feel impossible

**"Hearers only"** are often people whose **physical and mental state** prevents them from becoming **"doers."**

> **James 1:22** - "But be doers of the word, and not hearers only, deceiving yourselves."

This is not to condemn those who struggle—but to show the importance of preparation. **You cannot will yourself into obedience if your brain lacks the biochemical foundation to sustain it.** This is why:

- Sugar crashes create emotional instability that triggers defensiveness when truth challenges tradition
- Caffeine dependence suppresses the frontal lobe's ability to reason through complex prophecy
- Dopamine addiction makes 30 minutes of Bible study feel unbearably boring compared to social media
- Gut inflammation affects serotonin production, weakening emotional resilience needed to stand alone

**God asks us to love Him with all our heart, soul, mind, and strength** (Mark 12:30). When diet and media have compromised your mind and strength, loving God fully becomes neurologically difficult.

### Prepare Your Whole Being for This Truth

> **1 Thessalonians 5:23** - "Now may the God of peace Himself sanctify you completely; and may your whole spirit, soul, and body be preserved blameless at the coming of our Lord Jesus Christ."

**Spirit, soul, and body are interconnected:**
- **Body** (diet) affects **soul** (mind/emotions) affects **spirit** (discernment/obedience)
- You cannot separate physical health from spiritual faithfulness
- God calls us to be **wholly** prepared—not just intellectually convinced

**This is why Daniel refused the king's food BEFORE facing the test.** He understood what many miss:

**Physical discipline prepares you for spiritual obedience.**

Daniel didn't wait until the golden image was erected to start preparing. He laid the foundation in Daniel 1 (diet) so that when the test came in Daniel 3 (worship the image or die), his mind was clear, his will was strong, and his faith was unshakeable.

**The same principle applies today.** If you wait until Sunday laws are enforced to start preparing physically and mentally, it will be too late. The preparation must happen now:

1. **Restore your brain** (Daniel Diet) - so you can think clearly when deception intensifies
2. **Protect your mind** (Media Influence) - so you can resist propaganda and remain spiritually sensitive
3. **Understand the truth** (Babylon's Wine) - so you know what you're standing for when persecution comes

**This reading series is not just information—it's preparation for the final crisis.** Each guide builds the foundation the next one requires. Don't skip steps. Your eternal destiny may depend on the clarity of mind and strength of will you're building today.

> **Quick-reference companion**: [**Commandments.md**](Commandments.md) provides a standalone comparison of the Biblical, Catholic, and Protestant Ten Commandments with full Catholic and Protestant admissions. Share it with anyone who needs a focused introduction to the law-change question without reading the full series.
